Divine Decree
beginner
5 min
The Jabriyya View: Human Action as Mere Location
Jahm ibn Safwan denies real human action, attributing it as mere locus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Jabriyya position that human actions are only metaphorically attributed to humans as loci, not as real agents.

Core Idea
Humans are the place of action, not its source.

Before we can analyze the Maturidi position on human action, we must first understand the view they opposed. This passage presents the radical determinist position of Jahm ibn Safwan and the Jabriyya, who argued that human actions are not truly ours. Their reasoning hinges on a distinction between the originator of an action and its mere location.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the question posed and the immediate answer given by Jahm.
The passage is short but dense with theological import.
2
Distinguish between two types of attribution
Identify the key distinction: attribution to a place (mahall) vs attribution to an originator (muhassil). Jahm says human actions are like 'the wall moves' — the wall is the location, not the mover.
This analogy is central to understanding Jabriyya thought.
3
Identify the school and its followers
Note that Jahm ibn Safwan is the founder of the Jabriyya, who supported him. Recognize that this is one extreme of the qadar debate.
The Jabriyya are often contrasted with the Qadariyya who affirm complete human agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من موجد فعل العبد؟
واختلف الناس فيها فزعم جهم بن صفوان أن لا فعل للعبد في الحقيقة وما يضاف إليهم يضاف على حسب إضافة الأشياء إلى محالها دون إضافتها إلى محصلها، وساعده على هذه المقالة أصحابه وهم الجبرية.
From whom is the action of the servant? And the people differed concerning it. Jahm ibn Safwan claimed that the servant has no action in reality, and what is attributed to them is attributed according to the attribution of things to their places, not their attribution to their originator. His followers, the Jabriyya, supported him in this statement.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage introduces the foundational issue of the creation of human actions (khalq af'al al-'ibad). The author first poses a question: 'From whom is the action of the servant?' Then he states that people differed on this. He presents the first opinion: that of Jahm ibn Safwan. According to Jahm, the servant has no real action (la fi'l lil-'abd fi al-haqiqa). Any action attributed to humans is merely an attribution similar to the attribution of things to their locations (mahall) rather than their originator (muhassil). This means that just as we say 'the wall moves' when it is moved by an external cause, so too the human action is metaphorically attributed to the human as the locus, not the true agent. The true agent is only God. This view is supported by his followers, the Jabriyya, who are known for denying human free will and capability (istita'a).

Key Terms
فعل
عبد
جبرية
جهم بن صفوان
إضافة
محل
محصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think the Jabriyya completely deny any human role in action, leaving humans entirely passive like a stone.
Correction: The Jabriyya do not deny that actions appear in humans; they deny that humans are the true agents. They attribute actions to humans as loci, not as originators. Humans are not passive objects but are the location where God's creative power manifests.

Checkpoint
According to Jahm ibn Safwan, how is the action of a human being related to the human?
A) The human creates the action
B) The human is the true agent
C) The action is attributed to the human only as a location
D) The action is a combination of human and divine will

Key Takeaway
Jahm ibn Safwan and the Jabriyya hold that human actions are only attributed to humans as locations, not as true originators.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, is there a part of you that blames Allah's decree for your failure? This lesson shows the Jabriyya took that to an extreme. Would you rather be a passive victim of destiny or own your actions? Confront that tendency right now and decide to take responsibility.
?
If you truly believed that every action you do is merely a location where Allah acts, would you feel any personal accountability for your sins? How does the Jabriyya view challenge the very concept of repentance? Are you comfortable with the idea that your 'choice' might be an illusion? Write down one area of your life where you need to assert your agency.
?
Imagine standing before Allah on Judgment Day being asked about your actions. Would you dare to say, 'I was just the place where You created the deed'? If not, then how must you live today? Resolve to act as a true servant who chooses obedience, not a passive locus.

Divine Decree
beginner
4 min
The Foundation and the Jabriyya Denial
Introduces the issue and the Jabriyya position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core question of the creation of human acts and the extreme determinist position of the Jabriyya.

Core Idea
Jabriyya denies any real human action; only God truly acts.

This lesson introduces the central theological problem of human agency. The author first frames the question 'Who originates the servant's act?' and then presents the first answer: the Jabriyya, led by Jahm ibn Safwan, who claim that humans have no real act at all. This sets the stage for the opposing views that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note how the author frames the issue before presenting the Jabriyya view.
The passage connects this issue to divine attributes.
2
Identify the Jabriyya claim
Find where Jahm ibn Safwan's position is stated: that the servant has no real act, only a locus for God's action.
Contrast 'attribution to a locus' vs 'attribution to an agent'.
3
Reflect on implications
Consider what this view implies for moral responsibility and divine justice. Why might this be problematic?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
2- [مسائل التعديل والتجوير] الأصل في هذه المسائل مسألة خلق أفعال العباد وهي مبنية على ما مما يتعلق بصفات الله تعالى ويدخل تحتها على ما نبين. من موجد فعل العبد؟ واختلف الناس فيها فزعم جهم بن صفوان أن لا فعل للعبد في الحقيقة وما يضاف إليهم يضاف على حسب إضافة الأشياء إلى محالها دون إضافتها إلى محصلها، وساعده على هذه المقالة أصحابه وهم الجبرية. وقال من سواهم من فرق الأمة بأن العبد مكتسب على الحقيقة وله فعل إلا الأشعري، فإنه زعم أن العبد يسمى مكتسبا عاملا ولا يسمى فاعلاً، والفاعل في الحقيقة هو الله تعالى. ثم القائلون بأن العبد له فعل وكسب وعمل اختلفوا من موجد أفعال العباد؟ فزعمت القدرية أن موجدها على الحقيقة هو العبد ولا صنع الله تعالى ولا تصرف في فعل العبد البتة بوجه من الوجوه، غير أن أوائلهم كانوا لا يتجاسرون على إطلاق اسم الخالق على العباد، وكانوا يقولون : إنه موجد فعله ومحدثه ولا يقولون خالقه، وكانوا يساعدون أهل الحق على أن لا خالق إلا الله تعالى إلى أن نشأ بينهم الجبائي فرأى أن لا فرق بين اسم الخالق والموجد فزعم أن كل ما دب ودرج خالق لفعله الاختياري، فلما انتهت نوبة رياستهم إلى أبي عبد الله البصري الملقب بجعل زعم أن الخالق على الحقيقة هو العبد والله تعالى يسمى خالقا على مجاز القول دون الحقيقة. وقال أهل الحق : إن موجدها وخالقها على الحقيقة هو الله تعالى والعبد مكتسب له فاعل له، وساعدهم عليه متكلمو أهل الحديث والنجارية.
2. [Issues of Justice and Injustice] The foundation of these issues is the question of the creation of the acts of servants, and it is based on what pertains to the attributes of Allah, and under it fall [various matters] as we will explain. Who is the originator of the act of the servant? People differed concerning it. Jahm ibn Safwan claimed that the servant has no act in reality, and what is attributed to them is attributed by way of attributing things to their loci, not by way of attributing them to their agent. His followers agreed with him, and they are the Jabriyya. Those other than him from the sects of the community said that the servant is an acquirer (muktasib) in reality and has an act, except for al-Ash'ari, for he claimed that the servant is called an acquirer and a doer ('amil) but not an agent (fa'il), and the agent in reality is Allah. Then those who said that the servant has an act, acquisition, and work differed concerning who is the originator of the acts of servants? The Qadariyya claimed that their originator in reality is the servant, and there is no act of Allah nor any disposition in the act of the servant at all in any way, except that their early ones did not dare to apply the name of creator to the servants, and they used to say: he is the originator of his act and the innovator of it, and they did not say he is its creator, and they used to assist the People of Truth in that there is no creator except Allah, until al-Jubba'i arose among them and saw no difference between the name creator and originator, so he claimed that everything that crawls and walks is the creator of its voluntary act. When the turn of their leadership reached Abu 'Abd Allah al-Basri, nicknamed Ju'ul, he claimed that the creator in reality is the servant, and Allah is called creator metaphorically, not in reality. The People of Truth said: its originator and creator in reality is Allah, and the servant is an acquirer of it and an agent of it, and the theologians of the People of Hadith and the Najjariyya assisted them.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage presents the main schools of thought on the problem of human action. It begins by identifying the core issue: the creation of acts of servants, which relates to divine attributes. The author then poses the question: who originates the act of the servant? He then outlines the positions of various groups. First, Jahm ibn Safwan and the Jabriyya deny that the servant has any real act; actions are attributed to the servant only as a location, not as an agent. Second, most sects affirm that the servant is an acquirer (muktasib) and has an act, with the exception of al-Ash'ari, who says the servant is called an acquirer and a doer but not an agent (fa'il); the real agent is God. Third, the Qadariyya hold that the servant is the real originator of his act, with no divine involvement. The passage traces the evolution of Qadari thought: early Qadariyya avoided calling the servant 'creator', but al-Jubba'i equated 'originator' and 'creator', and later Abu 'Abd Allah al-Basri explicitly claimed that the servant is the real creator and God is only metaphorically called creator. Finally, the People of Truth (Ahl al-Haqq) assert that God is the real originator and creator, while the servant is the acquirer and agent, and this view is supported by the theologians of the Ahl al-Hadith and the Najjariyya. The passage thus provides a clear spectrum of positions from absolute determinism to human self-creation, with the Ash'ari and Maturidi positions mediating.

Key Terms
خلق أفعال العباد
جبرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume all Muslims agree that humans have free will and create their own actions.
Correction: This passage shows that the Jabriyya (early determinists) denied any real human act, a view that existed in early Islam.

Checkpoint
According to Jahm ibn Safwan, actions attributed to humans are attributed as...
A) agents who truly create them
B) loci or locations, not agents
C) partners with God in creation
D) metaphorical agents with no reality

Key Takeaway
The Jabriyya view that humans have no real act is the first major position on the creation of actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that every action you do is only attributed to you as a location, not as an agent, would you feel less responsible for your sins? Would that comfort you or trouble you? Look at your own heart: are you willing to be accountable for deeds you didn't truly cause?
?
When you sin, do you find yourself making excuses like 'God made me do it' or 'I couldn't help it'? In what ways might the Jabriyya mindset lurk in your own thinking, and what would it mean to take full ownership of your actions before Allah?
?
The Jabriyya view makes God the sole agent of all acts, including evil. Read the passage again: 'the servant has no act in reality.' If this were true, how would you justify Allah's justice in punishing sinners? Can you hold this view and still believe He is just? Why or why not?

The Ash'ari Middle Position
Presents the Ash'ari position on human action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari distinction between 'acquisition' (kasb) and 'agency' (fi'l), and why the servant is not called a true agent.

Core Idea
Ash'ari says the servant acquires an act but does not create it; God is the sole agent.

This lesson presents the Ash'ari view, which occupies a middle ground between full human agency and complete determinism. The author notes that most sects affirm that the servant is a 'muktasib' (acquirer), but al-Ash'ari adds a crucial nuance: the servant is called a doer but not an agent (fa'il).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the distinction between 'muktasib' (acquirer) and 'fa'il' (agent).
The term 'muktasib' is central.
2
Compare with Jabriyya
How is this different from Jahm's view? Ash'ari affirms a real acquisition, but denies the servant is a creator.
3
Question the terminology
Why might al-Ash'ari allow 'doer' ('amil) but not 'agent' (fa'il)? Think about the implications for responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
2- [مسائل التعديل والتجوير] الأصل في هذه المسائل مسألة خلق أفعال العباد وهي مبنية على ما مما يتعلق بصفات الله تعالى ويدخل تحتها على ما نبين. من موجد فعل العبد؟ واختلف الناس فيها فزعم جهم بن صفوان أن لا فعل للعبد في الحقيقة وما يضاف إليهم يضاف على حسب إضافة الأشياء إلى محالها دون إضافتها إلى محصلها، وساعده على هذه المقالة أصحابه وهم الجبرية. وقال من سواهم من فرق الأمة بأن العبد مكتسب على الحقيقة وله فعل إلا الأشعري، فإنه زعم أن العبد يسمى مكتسبا عاملا ولا يسمى فاعلاً، والفاعل في الحقيقة هو الله تعالى. ثم القائلون بأن العبد له فعل وكسب وعمل اختلفوا من موجد أفعال العباد؟ فزعمت القدرية أن موجدها على الحقيقة هو العبد ولا صنع الله تعالى ولا تصرف في فعل العبد البتة بوجه من الوجوه، غير أن أوائلهم كانوا لا يتجاسرون على إطلاق اسم الخالق على العباد، وكانوا يقولون : إنه موجد فعله ومحدثه ولا يقولون خالقه، وكانوا يساعدون أهل الحق على أن لا خالق إلا الله تعالى إلى أن نشأ بينهم الجبائي فرأى أن لا فرق بين اسم الخالق والموجد فزعم أن كل ما دب ودرج خالق لفعله الاختياري، فلما انتهت نوبة رياستهم إلى أبي عبد الله البصري الملقب بجعل زعم أن الخالق على الحقيقة هو العبد والله تعالى يسمى خالقا على مجاز القول دون الحقيقة. وقال أهل الحق : إن موجدها وخالقها على الحقيقة هو الله تعالى والعبد مكتسب له فاعل له، وساعدهم عليه متكلمو أهل الحديث والنجارية.
2. [Issues of Justice and Injustice] The foundation of these issues is the question of the creation of the acts of servants, and it is based on what pertains to the attributes of Allah, and under it fall [various matters] as we will explain. Who is the originator of the act of the servant? People differed concerning it. Jahm ibn Safwan claimed that the servant has no act in reality, and what is attributed to them is attributed by way of attributing things to their loci, not by way of attributing them to their agent. His followers agreed with him, and they are the Jabriyya. Those other than him from the sects of the community said that the servant is an acquirer (muktasib) in reality and has an act, except for al-Ash'ari, for he claimed that the servant is called an acquirer and a doer ('amil) but not an agent (fa'il), and the agent in reality is Allah. Then those who said that the servant has an act, acquisition, and work differed concerning who is the originator of the acts of servants? The Qadariyya claimed that their originator in reality is the servant, and there is no act of Allah nor any disposition in the act of the servant at all in any way, except that their early ones did not dare to apply the name of creator to the servants, and they used to say: he is the originator of his act and the innovator of it, and they did not say he is its creator, and they used to assist the People of Truth in that there is no creator except Allah, until al-Jubba'i arose among them and saw no difference between the name creator and originator, so he claimed that everything that crawls and walks is the creator of its voluntary act. Commentary

Checkpoint
What title does al-Ash'ari deny to the servant?
A) Muktasib (acquirer)
B) 'Ami (doer)
C) Fa'il (agent)
D) Khalq (creator)

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari view introduces a nuanced terminology to affirm both human responsibility and divine omnipotence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is the sole agent (fa'il) and you are only an acquirer (muktasib), how does that change the way you view your own successes and failures? Are you truly humble before God, or do you still secretly credit yourself as the ultimate cause? Name one area where you must repent of attributing agency to yourself.
?
Ash'ari says you are called a 'doer' but not an 'agent'. Does this distinction matter to your daily life? When you sin, do you feel the weight of your own responsibility, or do you subtly blame God's decree? In your prayer, do you beg God to change your heart as the only true agent?
?
The passage says the servant is an 'acquirer in reality'. If your actions are real, then your choices matter eternally. Are you living as though your choices have real weight, or do you use predestination as an excuse for spiritual laziness? What is one choice today you must make with full accountability?

The Qadariyya and the Rise of Human Autonomy
Traces the evolution of Qadariyya views on the origin of human acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will trace the evolution of Qadari thought from affirming human origination to claiming full creation by the servant, culminating in Abu 'Abd Allah al-Basri's extreme view.

Core Idea
Qadariyya evolved from moderate origination to claiming the servant is the real creator, even of God metaphorically.

This lesson follows the internal development of the Qadariyya. The author shows how their position shifted over time: early Qadariyya affirmed that the servant originates his act but avoided calling him 'creator', while later figures like al-Jubba'i and Abu 'Abd Allah al-Basri boldly declared the servant to be the true creator, reducing God's role to a mere metaphor.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the three stages: early Qadariyya, al-Jubba'i, and al-Basri.
The passage explicitly contrasts their views.
2
Identify the shifts
What did the early ones say? How did al-Jubba'i change it? What was al-Basri's claim?
Key terms: موجد, خالق, مجاز.
3
Analyze the trajectory
Notice how the Qadariyya became bolder over time, eventually denying God's real creative role in human acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
2- [مسائل التعديل والتجوير] الأصل في هذه المسائل مسألة خلق أفعال العباد وهي مبنية على ما مما يتعلق بصفات الله تعالى ويدخل تحتها على ما نبين. من موجد فعل العبد؟ واختلف الناس فيها فزعم جهم بن صفوان أن لا فعل للعبد في الحقيقة وما يضاف إليهم يضاف على حسب إضافة الأشياء إلى محالها دون إضافتها إلى محصلها، وساعده على هذه المقالة أصحابه وهم الجبرية. وقال من سواهم من فرق الأمة بأن العبد مكتسب على الحقيقة وله فعل إلا الأشعري، فإنه زعم أن العبد يسمى مكتسبا عاملا ولا يسمى فاعلاً، والفاعل في الحقيقة هو الله تعالى. ثم القائلون بأن العبد له فعل وكسب وعمل اختلفوا من موجد أفعال العباد؟ فزعمت القدرية أن موجدها على الحقيقة هو العبد ولا صنع الله تعالى ولا تصرف في فعل العبد البتة بوجه من الوجوه، غير أن أوائلهم كانوا لا يتجاسرون على إطلاق اسم الخالق على العباد، وكانوا يقولون : إنه موجد فعله ومحدثه ولا يقولون خالقه، وكانوا يساعدون أهل الحق على أن لا خالق إلا الله تعالى إلى أن نشأ بينهم الجبائي فرأى أن لا فرق بين اسم الخالق والموجد فزعم أن كل ما دب ودرج خالق لفعله الاختياري، فلما انتهت نوبة رياستهم إلى أبي عبد الله البصري الملقب بجعل زعم أن الخالق على الحقيقة هو العبد والله تعالى يسمى خالقا على مجاز القول دون الحقيقة. وقال أهل الحق : إن موجدها وخالقها على الحقيقة هو الله تعالى والعبد مكتسب له فاعل له، وساعدهم عليه متكلمو أهل الحديث والنجارية.
2. [Issues of Justice and Injustice] The foundation of these issues is the question of the creation of the acts of servants, and it is based on what pertains to the attributes of Allah, and under it fall [various matters] as we will explain. Who is the originator of the act of the servant? People differed concerning it. Jahm ibn Safwan claimed that the servant has no act in reality, and what is attributed to them is attributed by way of attributing things to their loci, not by way of attributing them to their agent. His followers agreed with him, and they are the Jabriyya. Those other than him from the sects of the community said that the servant is an acquirer (muktasib) in reality and has an act, except for al-Ash'ari, for he claimed that the servant is called an acquirer and a doer ('amil) but not an agent (fa'il), and the agent in reality is Allah. Then those who said that the servant has an act, acquisition, and work differed concerning who is the originator of the acts of servants? The Qadariyya claimed that their originator in reality is the servant, and there is no act of Allah nor any disposition in the act of the servant at all in any way, except that their early ones did not dare to apply the name of creator to the servants, and they used to say: he is the originator of his act and the innovator of it, and they did not say he is its creator, and they used to assist the People of Truth in that there is no creator except Allah, until al-Jubba'i arose among them and saw no difference between the name creator and originator, so he claimed that everything that crawls and walks is the creator of its voluntary act. When the turn of their leadership reached Abu 'Abd Allah al-Basri, nicknamed Ju'ul, he claimed that the creator in reality is the servant, and Allah is called creator metaphorically, not in reality. The People of Truth said: its originator and creator in reality is Allah, and the servant is an acquirer of it and an agent of it, and the theologians of the People of Hadith and the Najjariyya assisted them.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage presents the main schools of thought on the problem of human action. It begins by identifying the core issue: the creation of acts of servants, which relates to divine attributes. The author then poses the question: who originates the act of the servant? He then outlines the positions of various groups. First, Jahm ibn Safwan and the Jabriyya deny that the servant has any real act; actions are attributed to the servant only as a location, not as an agent. Second, most sects affirm that the servant is an acquirer (muktasib) and has an act, with the exception of al-Ash'ari, who says the servant is called an acquirer and a doer but not an agent (fa'il); the real agent is God. Third, the Qadariyya hold that the servant is the real originator of his act, with no divine involvement. The passage traces the evolution of Qadari thought: early Qadariyya avoided calling the servant 'creator', but al-Jubba'i equated 'originator' and 'creator', and later Abu 'Abd Allah al-Basri explicitly claimed that the servant is the real creator and God is only metaphorically called creator. Finally, the People of Truth (Ahl al-Haqq) assert that God is the real originator and creator, while the servant is the acquirer and agent, and this view is supported by the theologians of the Ahl al-Hadith and the Najjariyya. The passage thus provides a clear spectrum of positions from absolute determinism to human self-creation, with the Ash'ari and Maturidi positions mediating.

Key Terms

خالق

أبو عبد الله البصري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think all Qadariyya held the same view on human creation of actions.
Correction: The passage shows a clear evolution from moderate origination to explicit denial of God's creative role in human acts.

Checkpoint
Who among the following claimed that Allah is called creator only metaphorically?
A) Early Qadariyya
B) Al-Jubba'i
C) Abu 'Abd Allah al-Basri
D) Jahm ibn Safwan

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya evolved from moderate origination to extreme human self-creation, with each generation bolder than the last.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even momentarily, felt that your achievements were entirely your own doing, forgetting that Allah is the ultimate creator of your actions? How does the Qadariyya's slide into extreme self-reliance serve as a warning for your own heart? What concrete step can you take today to acknowledge Allah's creative role in your choices?
?
When you sin, do you blame yourself as if you are the sole creator of that act, independent of Allah's will? How can you reconcile sincere repentance with the belief that Allah's decree encompasses even your failures? Write one prayer that expresses both your responsibility and your reliance on Allah.
?
The Qadariyya ended up saying that Allah is only metaphorically the creator of human acts. Is there any area of your life where you act as if Allah's control is merely metaphorical—where you trust your own planning more than His decree? What would it look like to surrender that area to Him today?

The People of Truth: Divine Creation with Human Acquisition
States the Ahl al-Haqq position and its supporters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Haqq position that God is the sole creator of actions while the servant is the acquirer and agent, and who supported this view.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Haqq affirms God as the real creator and the servant as the acquirer and agent.

This lesson presents the concluding position of the passage: the People of Truth (Ahl al-Haqq) — likely the Maturidi and Ash'ari mainstream — who assert that God is the true originator and creator of all actions, while the servant is the acquirer (muktasib) and agent (fa'il). This view is supported by the theologians of Ahl al-Hadith and the Najjariyya.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two-part claim: God creates, servant acquires and acts.
2
Identify the supporters
The passage states that the People of Truth were assisted by the theologians of Ahl al-Hadith and the Najjariyya. Who are these groups?
3
Contrast with previous views
Compare this view with the Jabriyya, Ash'ari, and Qadariyya positions. How does it differ?

2- [مسائل التعديل والتجوير] الأصل في هذه المسائل مسألة خلق أفعال العباد وهي مبنية على ما مما يتعلق بصفات الله تعالى ويدخل تحتها على ما نبين. من موجد فعل العبد؟ واختلف الناس فيها فزعم جهم بن صفوان أن لا فعل للعبد في الحقيقة وما يضاف إليهم يضاف على حسب إضافة الأشياء إلى محالها دون إضافتها إلى محصلها، وساعده على هذه المقالة أصحابه وهم الجبرية. وقال من سواهم من فرق الأمة بأن العبد مكتسب على الحقيقة وله فعل إلا الأشعري، فإنه زعم أن العبد يسمى مكتسبا عاملا ولا يسمى فاعلاً، والفاعل في الحقيقة هو الله تعالى. ثم القائلون بأن العبد له فعل وكسب وعمل اختلفوا من موجد أفعال العباد؟ فزعمت القدرية أن موجدها على الحقيقة هو العبد ولا صنع الله تعالى ولا تصرف في فعل العبد البتة بوجه من الوجوه، غير أن أوائلهم كانوا لا يتجاسرون على إطلاق اسم الخالق على العباد، وكانوا يقولون : إنه موجد فعله ومحدثه ولا يقولون خالقه، وكانوا يساعدون أهل الحق على أن لا خالق إلا الله تعالى إلى أن نشأ بينهم الجبائي فرأى أن لا فرق بين اسم الخالق والموجد فزعم أن كل ما دب ودرج خالق لفعله الاختياري، فلما انتهت نوبة رياستهم إلى أبي عبد الله البصري الملقب بجعل زعم أن الخالق على الحقيقة هو العبد والله تعالى يسمى خالقا على مجاز القول دون الحقيقة. وقال أهل الحق : إن موجدها وخالقها على الحقيقة هو الله تعالى والعبد مكتسب له فاعل له، وساعدهم عليه متكلمو أهل الحديث والنجارية.

Quranic Proof for Istita'at al-Asbab wa al-Alat
Nasafi provides Quranic proofs for the capacity of means and instruments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran distinguishes between true power (qudra) and the capacity of means and instruments, and how Maturidi scholars use specific verses to prove the existence of istita'at al-asbab wa al-alat.

Core Idea
The Quran uses 'istita'a' to mean external means (health, wealth), not just metaphysical power.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla presents the Quranic evidence for one of the two types of capacity (istita'a) discussed in Maturidi kalam. While the Mu'tazila considered capacity as a single metaphysical power accompanying the act, Maturidis argued for a second type: the capacity of means and instruments (health, wealth, opportunity). The author cites four Quranic verses to demonstrate that 'istita'a' in these contexts refers to external, mundane prerequisites rather than the inner power to act. As you read, notice how each verse is used to argue that the common people's understanding of 'capacity' matches the Maturidi view.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two types of capacity
Before reading the proof, remember that Maturidi scholars divide istita'a into two: haqiqat al-qudra (true power of action) and istita'at al-asbab wa al-alat (capacity of means and instruments). The second is mundane and relates to health, wealth, and opportunity.
The Mu'tazila denied this division.
2
Examine the first Quranic proof (al-Mujadilah 58:4)
The verse exempts one who cannot fast for two months from the zihar expiation. The author argues that the 'istita'a' here cannot be true power because true power for a two-month fast is inconceivable before starting, so it must be the capacity of sound health.
This argument uses the opponents' own premise that power does not persist.
3
Analyze the hypocrites' statement (al-Tawbah 9:42)
The hypocrites said, 'If we had the capacity, we would have gone out with you.' Allah declared them liars. If they meant true power (which was absent), they would not be liars. So they meant means (health/wealth), which they had.
The author further supports this with the context of the weak and sick being excused.
4
Confirm with verses on marriage and pilgrimage (al-Nisa 4:25 and Al Imran 3:97)
Both use 'istita'a' in the context of financial and physical means—marriage requires wealth, pilgrimage requires provisions and transport. These reinforce the meaning of instrumental capacity.
The author concludes that these verses collectively prove the existence of istita'at al-asbab wa al-alat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الدليل على انقسام الاستطاعة إلى قسمين قوله تعالى: فَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مِسْكِينًا والمراد منه استطاعة الأسباب والآلات إذ لا يتصور وجود قدرة أداء صوم شهرين من قبل الشروع في أدائه، ويستحيل بقاء القدرة التي كانت موجودة عند الخصوم إلى شهرين، فدل أنه أراد به استطاعة سلامة الأسباب وصحة الآلات.
والدليل عليه ما عير الله تعالى به من قال من أهل النفاق: لَوِ اسْتَطَعْنَا لَخَرَجْنَا مَعَكُمْ وكذبهم الله تعالى في ذلك القول، ولو كانوا أرادوا بذلك الكلام الاستطاعة التي هي حقيقة قدرة الفعل ما كانوا بنفيها عن أنفسهم كاذبين، إذ لا شك أن استطاعة فعل الجهاد لا تبقى من وقت كونهم بالمدينة إلى أن يلقوا العدو ويباشروا القتال، وكان الخروج مطلوبًا لذلك، وحيث كذبهم دل أنهم أرادوا بذلك المرض أو فقد المال على ما بين الله تعالى بقوله: لَيْسَ عَلَى الضُّعَفَاءِ وَلَا عَلَى الْمَرْضَى إلى أن قال: إِنَّمَا السَّبِيلُ عَلَى الَّذِينَ يَسْتَذِنُونَكَ وَهُمْ أَغْنِيَاءُ.
ويحققه أن أهل النفاق كانوا عوام، وقدرة العمل التي توجب حصول الفعل ويتكلم فيها المتكلمون أنها مع الفعل أو قبله وتبقى أو لا تبقى مما لا يعرفه العوام ولا يصورونها في الأوهام، وذلك قوله تعالى: وَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ مِنكُمْ طَوْلًا والمراد به استطاعة الآلات، وكذا قوله تعالى: وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا والمراد به الزاد والراحلة لا حقيقة قدرة الفعل، فهذه الآيات دليل ثبوت استطاعة الأسباب والآلات.
Then the proof for the division of capacity into two types is His statement: "And who cannot afford [the fast], then a feeding of sixty poor people" and what is meant by it is the capacity of means and instruments, since it is inconceivable that the power to perform the fast of two months exists before beginning its performance, and it is impossible for the power that existed according to the opponents to last for two months. So it indicated that He intended by it the capacity of soundness of means and health of instruments.
And the proof for it is that Allah Almighty rebuked those among the hypocrites who said: "If we had the capacity, we would have gone out with you," and Allah Almighty declared them liars in that statement. Had they intended by that speech the capacity which is the true power of the act, they would not have been liars in denying it of themselves, for there is no doubt that the capacity to perform jihad does not remain from the time they were in Medina until they meet the enemy and engage in battle, and the departure was required for that. Since He declared them liars, it indicated that they intended by that illness or lack of wealth, as Allah Almighty explained with His statement: "There is no blame on the weak or the sick" up to His saying: "The way is only against those who ask permission of you while they are wealthy."
And what confirms it is that the hypocrites were common people, and the power of action that causes the occurrence of the act, which the theologians discuss (whether it is with the act or before it and whether it remains or does not remain), is something that common people do not know nor conceive in their minds. And that is His statement: "And whoever among you does not have the means [to marry free believing women]" and what is meant by it is the capacity of instruments. Likewise His statement: "And for Allah upon the people is the pilgrimage to the House, for whoever has the means to find a way to it" and what is meant by it is provision and mount, not the true power of the act. So these verses are proof of the existence of the capacity of means and instruments.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the existence of one of the two types of istita'a (capacity), namely istita'at al-asbab wa al-alat (capacity of means and instruments). The author begins by stating that the proof from the Quran is the verse from al-Mujadilah (58:4), which exempts one who cannot fast for two months from the expiation of zihar, requiring feeding sixty poor people instead. The argument is that the 'capacity' mentioned here cannot refer to the true power (qudra) to perform the fast, because that power would have to exist before starting the fast and persist for two months, which is impossible according to the opponents (the Mu'tazila) who deny the survival of power. Therefore, it must refer to the capacity of health and means. The author then provides a second proof from the story of the hypocrites in Surah at-Tawbah (9:42). The hypocrites said, 'If we had the capacity, we would have gone out with you,' and Allah declared them liars. If they meant true power (which they did not have), they would not be liars because true power for jihad does not persist from Medina to the battlefield. So they must have meant something else—illness or lack of means. This is confirmed by the subsequent verses that excuse the weak and sick. The author reinforces this with two more verses: an-Nisa (4:25) about marrying free believing women, and Al Imran (3:97) about pilgrimage, both using istita'a to mean means and instruments (like wealth and health), not metaphysical power. Thus, these verses collectively prove the existence of the capacity of means and instruments.

Key Terms
استطاعة
استطاعة الأسباب والآلات
حقيقة القدرة
كذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All instances of 'istita'a' in the Quran refer to the same metaphysical power (qudra).
Correction: Many Quranic verses use 'istita'a' to mean external means like health, wealth, and opportunity, distinct from the power to act.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why were the hypocrites considered liars when they said 'لو استطعنا لخرجنا معكم'?
A) They had the means (health and wealth) but claimed not to.
B) They meant true power, which they did not have, so they were truthful.
C) They were lying about their intention to go out.
D) Allah knew they were capable of fighting.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic usage of 'istita'a' often refers to external means, confirming the Maturidi division of capacity into true power and instrumental capacity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I can't' to an Islamic duty, do you honestly examine whether you lack the means (health, wealth, time) or are you hiding behind a vague excuse? This lesson shows Allah exposed the hypocrites' lie. What would He expose in your life?
?
The hypocrites had the wealth and health to join jihad but claimed they couldn't. Is there an obligation you've been avoiding—like seeking knowledge, giving charity, or reconciliation—where your 'can't' masks a 'won't'? Write down one specific way you will test your actual capacity this week.
?
This passage teaches that Allah distinguishes between true power (which is metaphysical) and instrumental capacity (which you can assess). Will you stop saying 'I don't have the strength' and instead ask: 'Do I have the health and resources? If so, what is stopping me?' Commit to answering that question honestly before your next prayer.

Quranic Proof for Istita'a as True Power
The author proves the existence of true capacity (qudra) using the verse from Hud and blame analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic verse from Surah Hud and the analysis of blame prove the existence of true capacity (qudra) distinct from external means and instruments.

Core Idea
True capacity (qudra) is the object of moral blame, not mere means.

This lesson examines the proof from Surah Hud for the reality of istita'a as true power. The author uses the verse 'They were not able to hear' to show that blame attaches to something internal, not just external faculties. We'll see how the argument distinguishes between lack of means and lack of true power, and why only the latter is blameworthy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation once. Notice the structure: a claim, a Quranic verse, and two confirmations (yuḥaqqiqahu).
The passage is dense but follows a clear logical progression.
2
Identify the two types of istita'a
The passage distinguishes between istita'a as means/instruments and istita'a as true power (qudra). Find where each is mentioned and note how the verse negates only the latter.
The means (hearing organs) were present, but true power was absent.
3
Understand the blame argument
The author argues that blame (dhamm) in the verse is only justified if the disbeliever lacked true power despite having sound means. If the lack were of means, blame would be unjust because that is not in one's control.
The blame is specific to the disbeliever, proving true power is the basis of moral responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هناك استطاعة بمعنى حقيقة القدرة:
وأما دليل ثبوت الاستطاعة التي هي حقيقة القدرة فقوله تعالى: مَا كَانُوا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ السَّمْعَ والمراد منه نفي حقيقة القدرة لا نفي الأسباب والآلات؛ لأنها كانت ثابتة، وإنما المنتفى عنهم كان حقيقة القدرة التي بها يتعلق الفعل.
ويحققه أنه ذكر ذلك على وجه الذم لهم، والذم إنما يلحقهم بانعدام حقيقة القدرة عند وجود الأسباب وصحة الآلات لا بانعدام سلامة الأسباب وصحة الآلات، لأن انتفاء تلك الاستطاعة لم تكن بتضييعه بل هو في ذلك مجبور، انتفاء حقيقة القدرة فموجب ذمهم؛ لأن انعدامها مع سلامة الأسباب وصحة الآلات كانت بتضييعه إياها لاشتغاله بضد ما أمر به.
ويحققه أنه خص بنفس هذه الاستطاعة الكافر، وانتفاء تلك الاستطاعة يستوي فيه المسلم والكافر، وإنما المختص بالكافر هو انتفاء هذه الاستطاعة، والدليل عليه قول صاحب موسى لموسى عليهما السلام: إِنَّكَ لَن تَسْتَطِيعَ مَعِيَ صَبْرًا
There is a capacity meaning true power:
As for the proof of the existence of the capacity which is true power, it is His statement: "They were not able to hear" and what is meant by it is the negation of true power, not the negation of means and instruments, because they were present. Rather, what was negated from them was the true power by which the act is attached.
And what confirms it is that He mentioned it as a blame upon them. Blame attaches to them only due to the absence of true power despite the existence of means and soundness of instruments, not due to the absence of soundness of means and health of instruments, because the absence of that capacity (of means) was not due to their own doing but they were compelled in that. The absence of true power is what necessitates blame upon them, because its absence despite soundness of means and health of instruments was due to their own doing by occupying themselves with the opposite of what they were commanded.
And what confirms it is that this capacity is specifically negated from the disbeliever. The absence of that capacity (of means) is the same for Muslim and disbeliever. Rather, what is specific to the disbeliever is the absence of this capacity. The proof for it is the statement of the companion of Moses to Moses, peace be upon them: "Indeed, you will not be able to have patience with me."
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the existence of the second type of istita'a, which is haqiqat al-qudra (true power). The author begins by stating that there is another meaning of istita'a, namely true power. The proof is the verse from Surah Hud (11:20): 'ما كانوا يستطيعون السمع' (They were not able to hear). The argument is that the negation here must be of true power, not of means and instruments, because the disbelievers had the means (hearing organs) but lacked the true capacity to hear the truth. This is proven by the fact that the verse is stated as a blame (dhamm) upon them. Blame is only deserved if they had the means but lacked the true power due to their own fault—otherwise, if the lack of means was not their doing, they would not be blamed. The author explains that the absence of means (like health) is not blameworthy because one is compelled in that. However, the absence of true power despite having means is blameworthy because it is due to their own negligence—they occupied themselves with what opposes the command. This shows that true power is something distinct from means and is the object of moral responsibility. To further clarify, the author points out that the absence of means (istita'at al-asbab) is common to both Muslim and disbeliever (e.g., both can be sick), but the absence of true power is specific to the disbeliever. This is substantiated by the story of Musa and Khidr (Al-Kahf 18:72), where Khidr tells Musa that he cannot (lan tastati'a) have patience with him, meaning the true capacity for patience is absent—not the means. Thus, the passage establishes the existence of a distinct capacity called true power (qudra) that is the basis for obligation and blame.

Key Terms
استطاعة بمعنى حقيقة القدرة
نفي حقيقة القدرة
ذم
تضييع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All instances of 'istita'a' in the Quran refer to external means and instruments.
Correction: This passage shows that some instances, like 'They were not able to hear,' refer to an internal true power (qudra) that is the basis of moral responsibility, as proven by the blame analysis.

Checkpoint
Why is the disbeliever blamed for the absence of true power according to the author?
A) Because he lacked the means of hearing.
B) Because he had the means but used them in disobedience, thus forfeiting true power.
C) Because true power is a gift that cannot be acquired.
D) Because the disbeliever is compelled to lack it.

Key Takeaway
True capacity (qudra) is proven by the Quranic verse and blame analysis as a distinct internal power that is the object of moral responsibility, separate from external means.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you disobey Allah, do you honestly examine whether you had the means but lacked the true inner capacity to obey? Think of a specific sin and pinpoint what was absent: Was it opportunity, or was it your resolve? Ask Allah to grant you the true power to obey next time.
?
The disbelievers are blamed because they occupied themselves with the opposite of what they were commanded. What are you currently occupying yourself with that is the opposite of what Allah commands? Commit to one concrete action today to realign your focus.
?
Moses was told he lacked the true capacity to be patient with Khidr despite having the means. In which relationship or situation do you find yourself impatient, and how might you be relying on mere means rather than seeking true capacity from Allah? Pray for it now.

The Definition and First Istita'a
Thumama and Bishr define istita'a, refute Dirar, and state consensus on first istita'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of istita'a as external conditions and the concept of the first istita'a which precedes action and is valid for opposites.

Core Idea
Istita'a is not a power but the soundness of limbs and means.

In this passage, the early Mu'tazili thinkers Thumama and Bishr define istita'a purely in terms of physical readiness. This material definition is used to refute Dirar's view that capacity is part of the person. Then the text reports consensus on the first istita'a which precedes action and is neutral toward good and evil.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
The passage begins with Thumama and Bishr's definition of istita'a. Read it carefully to understand their materialist view.
2
Understand the refutation
The author refutes Dirar and Hafs al-Fard by arguing that istita'a is an accident, not a part of the body. Accidents cannot be parts of bodies.
This is a key kalam argument about the nature of accidents.
3
Examine the consensus
The second part asserts that the first istita'a precedes the action. This means the capacity is present before the act, not simultaneous with it.
4
Reflect on the examples
Notice the examples: a sound hand can be used for jihad or fighting Muslims; a sound leg can go to mosques or to sinful places. This shows the first istita'a is neutral—valid for opposites.
This refutes the idea that capacity determines the moral quality of the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثمامة بن الأشرس وبشر بن المعتمر: أن الاستطاعة ليست غير سلامة الأسباب وصحة الجوارح وتخليها عن الآفات. وبهذا أيضا يبطل قول ضرار وحفص الفرد أنها بعض المستطيع لما ثبت أنها عرض، والقول بكون العرض بعض الجسم محال. والله الموفق. ثم أجمع القائلون بالاستطاعة المثبتون للعبد الأعمال أن الاستطاعة الأولى تتقدم الفعل [؟]، فإن اليد السليمة والرجل الصحيحة يتقدمان البطش والمشي، والزاد والراحلة يتقدمان وجود أفعال الحج، وكذلك يصلح للضدين، فإن اليد الصحيحة كما تصلح لجهاد الكفار تصلح لقتال أهل الإسلام، وكذا الرجل السليمة كما تصلح [؟] للمشي إلى المساجد تصلح للمشي إلى بيوت الخمارين والزواني.
Thumama ibn al-Ashras and Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir: that istita'a (capacity) is nothing other than the safety of causes and the soundness of limbs and their being free from defects. And by this also is invalidated the saying of Dirar and Hafs al-Fard that it is a part of the capable person, because it is established that it is an accident, and the assertion that an accident is a part of a body is impossible. And God is the giver of success. Then those who affirm istita'a and affirm actions for the servant are in consensus that the first istita'a precedes the action [؟], for the sound hand and the sound leg precede the strike and the walking, and the provision and the mount precede the existence of the actions of Hajj, and likewise it is valid for the two opposites, for the sound hand is as suitable for jihad against the disbelievers as it is suitable for fighting the people of Islam, and likewise the sound leg is as suitable [؟] for walking to the mosques as it is suitable for walking to the houses of wine-sellers and fornicators.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage begins by presenting the definition of istita'a (capacity) according to Thumama ibn al-Ashras and Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir: it is nothing but the safety of causes (salamat al-asbab) and the soundness of limbs (sihhat al-jawarih) and their being free from defects. This is a material definition that reduces capacity to external conditions. The author then uses this definition to refute Dirar and Hafs al-Fard, who claimed that capacity is a part of the capable person (ba'd al-mustati'). The refutation is that capacity is an accident ('arad), and an accident cannot be a part of a body, as that is impossible. After stating 'And God is the giver of success', the author reports a consensus among those who affirm both istita'a and actions for the servant: the first istita'a (al-istita'a al-ula) precedes the action. Examples are given: the sound hand and leg precede striking and walking; provisions and a mount precede the actions of Hajj. Furthermore, this first istita'a is valid for both opposites (salih li al-diddain): the same hand is suitable for both jihad against disbelievers and fighting Muslims; the same leg is suitable for walking to mosques or to houses of wine-sellers and fornicators. This establishes that the first istita'a, being only external readiness, does not determine the moral direction of the action.

سلامة الأسباب
صحة الجوارح
العرض
الاستطاعة الأولى
صالحة للضدين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think istita'a is a separate power or an actual part of the person.
Correction: The text shows it is merely external conditions (safety of causes and soundness of limbs) and is an accident, not a part.

Checkpoint
According to Thumama and Bishr, what is istita'a?
A) A power inherent in the soul
B) Safety of causes and soundness of limbs
C) A part of the capable person
D) A divine attribute

Key Takeaway
The first istita'a is merely physical readiness, not a moral determinant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your hand is sound. Where does it walk—to the mosque or to the house of sin? If the capacity is the same, what are you doing with your limbs that shows you are grateful to the One who gave them to you? Will you make a conscious choice today to use your sound limbs for an act of obedience instead of mere habit?
?
If your ability to do good or evil is nothing more than physical readiness, then what truly determines whether you use your provision for Hajj or for a sinful journey? Are you relying on your own soundness or on Allah's guidance to choose the right action? What will you change in your daily routine to ensure that your 'first istita'a' leads to what pleases Allah?
?
You have the same tongue, the same eyes, the same hands as the most righteous person. The capacity is identical. What is the difference between you and them? If it is not the capacity itself, then it must be something you are responsible for. What is that 'something' in your life right now that you are neglecting? Will you leave this lesson without addressing it?

The Second Istita'a: Simultaneous with Action
Al-Nasafi presents the dispute on the timing of the second istita'a and the Maturidi proof from accident theory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi school holds that the second istita'a must be simultaneous with the action and cannot precede it.

Core Idea
Power is an accident; accidents cannot persist, so power must be at the moment of action.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents a key theological disagreement about the timing of human power (istita'a). While some schools argue that power must come before the action, the Maturidi tradition insists on simultaneity. The argument is grounded in the nature of accidents and their inability to endure over time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the two positions
Read the Arabic and translation once. Identify the two opposing views: (1) Mu'tazila and Dirariyya claim power precedes, (2) Maturidis and others claim it is simultaneous.
This sets up the debate.
2
Examine the proof from the nature of accidents
The Maturidi argument hinges on a key premise: al-qudra al-haditha is an accident, and accidents cannot persist. Trace how this leads to the conclusion.
Focus on the logical chain: power as accident → cannot persist → if it preceded, it would perish → action without power → impossible.
3
Reflect on the theological consequences
Consider why the author mentions the impossibility of the world existing without God's power and an act without human capacity. How does this absurdity strengthen the argument?
Connects to broader principles of tawhid and human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الاستطاعة الثانية فقد اختلفوا في جواز تقدمها على الفعل، فزعمت المعتزلة والضرارية : أنها تكون سابقة على الفعل ويستحيل اقترانها به [؟]، وإليه ذهب أكثر الكرامية. وقال أصحابنا وجميع متكلمي أهل الحديث والنجارية: إنها تكون مع الفعل ومحال تقدمها على الفعل. وذلك لأن القدرة الحادثة عرض، والعرض يستحيل بقاؤه، فلو كانت القدرة سابقة على الفعل لانعدمت وقت الفعل فيكون فعل بدون قدرة وهذا مستحيل لأنه يترتب عليه وجود العالم بدون قدرة الله ووجود عمل للإنسان بدون استطاعته.
As for the second istita'a, they differed regarding the permissibility of its precedence over the action. The Mu'tazila and the Dirariyya claimed that it is prior to the action and it is impossible for it to be simultaneous with it [؟], and most of the Karramiyya inclined to that. And our companions (as-habuna) and all the mutakallimun of the people of hadith and the Najjariyya said: it is simultaneous with the action and its precedence over the action is impossible. That is because the originated power (al-qudra al-haditha) is an accident, and an accident cannot persist. If the power were to precede the action, it would cease to exist at the time of the action, so there would be an action without power, and this is impossible because it would entail the existence of the world without God's power and the existence of an act for a human without his capacity.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage presents the disagreement regarding the second istita'a or power (al-istita'a al-thaniya) – whether it can precede the action or must be simultaneous. The Mu'tazila and Dirariyya hold that it is prior to the action and cannot be simultaneous with it; most Karramiyya agree. In contrast, the author's school (As-habuna, i.e., the Maturidis), along with all mutakallimun of the hadith folk and the Najjariyya, maintain that the power is simultaneous with the action and cannot precede it. The proof is given: the originated power (al-qudra al-haditha) is an accident ('arad), and accidents cannot persist over time (istihalat baqa' al-'arad). Therefore, if the power were to exist before the action, it would have perished by the time the action occurs, resulting in an action without any power – which is impossible. Such impossibility is further reinforced by the absurd consequence that the world would exist without God's power and a human act would exist without the human's capacity. This argument ties the existence of power to the moment of the action, rejecting any temporal gap.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة الثانية
القدرة الحادثة
العرض
استحالة بقاء العرض
المعتزلة
الضرارية
الكرامية
النجارية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that human power must exist before an action in order to cause it.
Correction: The Maturidi school argues that power is an accident that cannot persist; therefore it must be simultaneous with the action, not prior.

Checkpoint
Why do the Maturidis hold that the second istita'a cannot precede the action?
A) Because the action would then be impossible
B) Because the power is an accident that cannot persist until the time of action
C) Because the Mu'tazila say otherwise
D) Because the Qur'an commands it

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi school proves that human power (second istita'a) must be simultaneous with the action because power is an accident that cannot persist over time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever delayed an act of worship because you felt you weren't 'ready' or didn't have the strength? If power is only at the moment of action, what is the spiritual danger of waiting for a feeling of readiness before you obey? Will you, today, perform one action you've been postponing, trusting that Allah will give you the power exactly when you start?
?
This lesson teaches that your ability to act is an accident that does not persist. Each action is a fresh creation from Allah. How does this truth strip away any pride you might have in your own achievements? What would it mean for your next prayer to begin with the realization that you have no power except from Him?
?
If you truly believe that action without God's power is impossible, how does that change the way you face a difficult task or sin? Are you willing to call upon Allah for that specific momentary power before every word and deed today?

Istita'a Valid for Opposites: Pre-Action View and Abu Hanifa's Substitution
Discusses the pre-action view and Abu Hanifa's substitution view on istita'a's validity for opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why those who place istita'a before action affirm its validity for opposites, and how Abu Hanifa's 'substitution' view offers a nuanced position within those who place it with the action.

Core Idea
Power can be valid for opposites by substitution, not simultaneously.

The discussion of whether istita'a (power) is valid for opposites is a central debate in kalam. In this passage, the author first presents the unanimous view of those who hold that istita'a precedes the action—they all affirm its validity for opposites. Then he introduces the split among those who hold that istita'a is simultaneous with the action, focusing on Abu Hanifa's unique 'substitution' position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the phrase 'ala tariq al-badal' which is key.
2
Identify the two main groups
The passage first states the view of those who place istita'a before action, then among those who place it with action, Abu Hanifa's view is given. Note how the first group all agree, while the second group is divided.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's substitution concept
Reflect on the meaning of 'substitution': the same power is valid for only one opposite when coupled with it, but could have been valid for the other if coupled differently. This is distinct from simultaneous validity.
This is a nuanced position avoiding absolute indifference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلفوا في كونها صالحة للضدين فقال جميع من زعم أن الاستطاعة قبل الفعل : إنها تصلح للضدين كما تصلح لذلك الأسباب والآلات. واختلف القائلون بأنها مع الفعل في ذلك فقال أبو حنيفة: إنها تصلح للضدين على طريق البدل، ومعنى ذلك أن الاستطاعة التي حصل بها الإيمان صلحت له ولا تصلح للكفر إذا اقترنت بالإيمان، ولكنها لو كانت اقترنت بالكفر بدلاً من اقترانها بالإيمان لصلحت له بدلاً من صلاحها للإيمان، وتابعه على هذا القول ابن الراوندي وأبو العباس القلانسي من متكلمي أهل الحديث [؟] وأبو العباس ابن سريج من فقهاء أصحاب الحديث. وقالت الأشعرية وجميع متكلمي أهل الحديث سوى القلانسي وابن سريج: إن القدرة لا تصلح للضدين، وإن قدرة الإيمان لا تصلح للكفر وهي غير قدرة الكفر وكذا على القلب، وكذا هذا من قدرة الطاعة وقدرة المعصية وهو قول الحسين بن محمد النجار.
And they differed regarding whether it is valid for the two opposites. Those who hold that istita'a is before the action said: it is valid for the two opposites, as the causes and instruments are valid for that. And those who say that it is simultaneous with the action differed regarding that. Abu Hanifa said: it is valid for the two opposites in the way of substitution (ala tariq al-badal), and the meaning of that is that the istita'a by which faith is obtained is valid for it and is not valid for disbelief when it is coupled with faith, but if it were to be coupled with disbelief instead of being coupled with faith, it would be valid for it instead of being valid for faith. And Ibn al-Rawandi and Abu al-Abbas al-Qalanisi from the mutakallimun of the people of hadith [؟] and Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj from the jurists of the people of hadith followed him in this view. And the Ash'ariyya and all the mutakallimun of the people of hadith except al-Qalanisi and Ibn Surayj said: the power is not valid for the two opposites; indeed, the power of faith is not valid for disbelief and it is other than the power of disbelief, and likewise the reverse, and likewise this applies to the power of obedience and the power of disobedience. And this is the view of al-Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Najjar.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage addresses the question of whether istita'a (power) is valid for both opposites (salih li al-diddain), i.e., can the same capacity be used for both good and evil actions. The first group, those who hold that istita'a precedes the action, all agree that it is valid for opposites, just as external causes and instruments can be used for either purpose. Among those who hold that istita'a is simultaneous with the action, there is a split. Abu Hanifa's view is presented first: he says the power is valid for opposites 'ala tariq al-badal' (by way of substitution). This means that the actual power that brings about faith is, when actually coupled with faith, only valid for faith and not for disbelief. However, if it had been coupled with disbelief instead, it would have been valid for disbelief. In other words, the same power is not simultaneously valid for both, but it could have been for the opposite had the context been different. This is a nuanced position. Abu Hanifa's followers include Ibn al-Rawandi, al-Qalanisi (a hadith theologian), and Ibn Surayj (a Shafi'i jurist). The second view is that of the Ash'aris and most hadith theologians (except al-Qalanisi and Ibn Surayj): the power is not valid for opposites at all. The power for faith is specifically for faith and is a different power from the power for disbelief; the same applies in reverse, and likewise for the power of obedience and disobedience. This view, as noted, is also held by al-Najjar. This reflects a strict occasionalist view where each power is created specifically for its actual effect.

Key Terms
صالحة للضدين
طريق البدل
استطاعة
أبو حنيفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if power is valid for opposites, it must be simultaneously valid for both.
Correction: Abu Hanifa's substitution view shows that the same power can be valid for only one opposite at a time, but could have been valid for the other had it been coupled with that opposite.

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when the power is coupled with faith, is it valid for disbelief?
A) Yes, simultaneously
B) No, but it would have been if coupled with disbelief instead
C) No, never
D) Yes, but only after faith ends

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's substitution view allows the same power to be valid for either opposite, but only one at a time, depending on which opposite it is coupled with.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own capacity to choose between good and evil, do you truly recognize that the same istita'a that enables your faith could have been used for disbelief had you turned it elsewhere? What does that vulnerability demand of your heart right now?
?
Abu Hanifa says your power is only valid for what it is actually coupled with. In which area of your life are you pretending that you have the capacity for both obedience and disobedience, and what would it look like to commit your istita'a entirely to faith today?
?
If the very power that brought you to faith is not neutral but becomes specific by your choice, then every moment you are defining your capacity. What specific action will you take in the next hour to ensure your istita'a is coupled with what pleases Allah, not just what feels easy?

Ash'ari and Hadith Scholars' Negation of Istita'a for Opposites
Presents Ash'ari and hadith scholars' view that power is not valid for opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position that power is not valid for opposites and that each power is specific to its effect.

Core Idea
Power for faith and power for disbelief are distinct created powers.

The Ash'aris and most hadith theologians take a strict view: the power that produces faith cannot produce disbelief, and vice versa. This reflects a strong occasionalist commitment where each event has its own particular power created by Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the emphatic language 'la tusalihu' (is not valid).
The passage lists three pairs: faith/disbelief, reverse, and obedience/disobedience.
2
Compare with Abu Hanifa's view
Contrast this passage with the previous one. Abu Hanifa allowed substitution; the Ash'aris deny any potential validity for the opposite. Understand the difference.
3
Understand the theological motivation
Ask: why would the Ash'aris insist on distinct powers? This is consistent with their occasionalist theology where every event is directly created by Allah, and no created capacity has inherent efficacy.
This view maintains that human power is created at the moment of action and is specific to that action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلفوا في كونها صالحة للضدين فقال جميع من زعم أن الاستطاعة قبل الفعل : إنها تصلح للضدين كما تصلح لذلك الأسباب والآلات. واختلف القائلون بأنها مع الفعل في ذلك فقال أبو حنيفة: إنها تصلح للضدين على طريق البدل، ومعنى ذلك أن الاستطاعة التي حصل بها الإيمان صلحت له ولا تصلح للكفر إذا اقترنت بالإيمان، ولكنها لو كانت اقترنت بالكفر بدلاً من اقترانها بالإيمان لصلحت له بدلاً من صلاحها للإيمان، وتابعه على هذا القول ابن الراوندي وأبو العباس القلانسي من متكلمي أهل الحديث [؟] وأبو العباس ابن سريج من فقهاء أصحاب الحديث. وقالت الأشعرية وجميع متكلمي أهل الحديث سوى القلانسي وابن سريج: إن القدرة لا تصلح للضدين، وإن قدرة الإيمان لا تصلح للكفر وهي غير قدرة الكفر وكذا على القلب، وكذا هذا من قدرة الطاعة وقدرة المعصية وهو قول الحسين بن محمد النجار.
And they differed regarding whether it is valid for the two opposites. Those who hold that istita'a is before the action said: it is valid for the two opposites, as the causes and instruments are valid for that. And those who say that it is simultaneous with the action differed regarding that. Abu Hanifa said: it is valid for the two opposites in the way of substitution (ala tariq al-badal), and the meaning of that is that the istita'a by which faith is obtained is valid for it and is not valid for disbelief when it is coupled with faith, but if it were to be coupled with disbelief instead of being coupled with faith, it would be valid for it instead of being valid for faith. And Ibn al-Rawandi and Abu al-Abbas al-Qalanisi from the mutakallimun of the people of hadith [؟] and Abu al-Abbas ibn Surayj from the jurists of the people of hadith followed him in this view. And the Ash'ariyya and all the mutakallimun of the people of hadith except al-Qalanisi and Ibn Surayj said: the power is not valid for the two opposites; indeed, the power of faith is not valid for disbelief and it is other than the power of disbelief, and likewise the reverse, and likewise this applies to the power of obedience and the power of disobedience. And this is the view of al-Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Najjar.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage addresses the question of whether istita'a (power) is valid for both opposites (salih li al-diddain), i.e., can the same capacity be used for both good and evil actions. The first group, those who hold that istita'a precedes the action, all agree that it is valid for opposites, just as external causes and instruments can be used for either purpose. Among those who hold that istita'a is simultaneous with the action, there is a split. Abu Hanifa's view is presented first: he says the power is valid for opposites 'ala tariq al-badal' (by way of substitution). This means that the actual power that brings about faith is, when actually coupled with faith, only valid for faith and not for disbelief. However, if it had been coupled with disbelief instead, it would have been valid for disbelief. In other words, the same power is not simultaneously valid for both, but it could have been for the opposite had the context been different. This is a nuanced position. Abu Hanifa's followers include Ibn al-Rawandi, al-Qalanisi (a hadith theologian), and Ibn Surayj (a Shafi'i jurist). The second view is that of the Ash'aris and most hadith theologians (except al-Qalanisi and Ibn Surayj): the power is not valid for opposites at all. The power for faith is specifically for faith and is a different power from the power for disbelief; the same applies in reverse, and likewise for the power of obedience and disobedience. This view, as noted, is also held by al-Najjar. This reflects a strict occasionalist view where each power is created specifically for its actual effect.

Key Terms
قدرة الإيمان
قدرة الكفر
الأشعرية
قدرة الطاعة
قدرة المعصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Ash'ari view is similar to Abu Hanifa's because both deny simultaneous validity
Correction: The Ash'aris deny any potential validity for the opposite, even by substitution; each power is created uniquely for its specific effect.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari view, is the power of faith the same as the power of disbelief?
A) Yes, but used differently
B) No, they are two distinct powers
C) Yes, by substitution
D) No, but they could be if Allah willed

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari view insists that each power is specific to its actual effect; no single power can be valid for opposites.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform an act of worship, do you ever feel a sense of pride in your own ability? How does the Ash'ari view that your power is a distinct creation from Allah challenge that feeling?
?
If the power for faith is separate from the power for disbelief, what does that say about your responsibility when you sin? Are you tempted to blame your lack of power, or does this teaching call you to examine your heart more deeply?
?
How does knowing that each of your actions is tied to a specific power created by Allah change the way you seek His help before making a choice between obedience and disobedience?
