حجة أهل الحق وردهم على المعتزلة]: والحجة لأهل الحق قوله تعالى : ( خَلِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ ) (۱) وأفعال العباد أشياء فيكون الله تعالى خالقها لعموم (۲) الآية، والخصوم يعترضون على ذلك فيقولون: أفعال العباد مخصوصة من هذه الآية بدليل غرض الآية، فإنها خرجت مخرج التمدح وبدخول أفعال العباد تحتها يزول معنى التمدح بل يثبت معنى يوجب الذم، وهذا لأن من جملة أفعال العباد ما هو افتراء على الله تعالى ووصف له بما لا يليق بصفاته وشتم له وقتل أوليائه، وبسط اليد واللسان في رسله وأنبيائه، ومقابله سفرائه إلى خلقه وأمنائه على وحيه ومبلغي (۳) أمره ونهيه بكل ما قدروا عليه من المكروه ووسعه طوقهم من الجفوة، والمتعرض لشتم نفسه والافتراء عليه سفه في الشاهد الذي هو دليل يبتنى عليه أمور الغائب، فكيف الموجد لذلك والمخرج له من راجع شرح مطالع الأنظار على الطوالع ص ۱۹۰ ومنها أن أفعالنا خلق لنا لأنها واقعة بحسب قصودنا وإرادتنا وامتناعنا منها إذا شئنا راجع التمهيد للباقلاني ص ۳۰۷ ومنها أن العبد مطالب من ربه بالطاعة ويستحيل في العقول أن يطالب العبد بما لا يقع منه. راجع الإرشاد للجويني ص ۲۰۳ . ومنها ما أخذوه من النقل مثل قوله تعالى: وَتَخلُقُونَ إفكًا * ويرد عليهم بأن المقصود وتختلقون كذبًا أي تتخرصون وتكذبون. ومنها قوله تعالى: تَخَلُقُ مِنَ الدِّينِ كَهَيْئَةِ الطَّيْرِ بِإِذْنِي فَتَنفُخُ فِيهَا فَتَكُونُ طَيرا بإذني ويرد بأن الخلق هنا بمعنى التقدير أي تقدر في قلبك . راجع التمهيد للباقلاني ص ٣٠٩ - ٣١٠. (۱) سورة الرعد - ١٣ - الآية ١٦. (۲) فإن قالوا: هذا الذي تمسكتم به عموم وللعلماء في الصيغ العامة مذهبان أحدهما جحد اقتضاء الألفاظ للعموم والثاني القول بالعموم مع المصير إلى تعرضه للتأويل وكل ظاهر متعرض لجهات الاحتمالات فلا يسوغ التمسك به في القطعيات. قلنا: لم نتمسك بمحض الصيغة حتى أوضحنا اقترانها بإرادة التمدح وبينا أن ذلك التمدح مفهوم من مقتضى الآية على قطع ولا يستمر حمل الآية على الخصوص مع ما استيقناه من التمدح والمفهوم وإن لم يستفد من مجرد الصيغ فهو متلقى من القرائن. فإن قالوا هي متروكة الظاهر فإن الظاهر يقتضي كون الرب خالق كل شيء واسم الشيء يطلق على القديم والمحدث. قلنا : المخاطب المتكلم في هذه المواضع لا يدخل تحت قضية الخطاب ولا تندرئ قواطع النصوص بالزوغان والحيل . راجع الشامل للجويني ص ١٩٨-١٩٩. (۳) لوحة ٢٥١ ظ ز .
The proof of the People of Truth and their refutation of the Mu'tazila: The proof for the People of Truth is His statement: 'He created everything.' And actions of servants are things, so Allah is their Creator, due to the generality of the verse. And the opponents object to that, saying: The actions of servants are excluded from this verse by the evidence of the purpose of the verse; for it came in the context of praise, and if actions of servants entered under it, the meaning of praise would vanish, rather a meaning requiring blame would be established. This is because among the actions of servants are slander against Allah, description of Him with what is not befitting His attributes, insult to Him, killing of His friends, extending hand and tongue against His messengers and prophets, and confronting His emissaries to His creation, His trustees over His revelation, and those who convey His command and prohibition with all the harm they could and the harshness they could afford. And the one who subjects himself to insult and slander is foolish in the witnessed world, which is a proof upon which matters of the unseen are based; so how about the one who creates that and brings it forth? Refer to Sharh Matali' al-Anzar... And among their doubts is that our actions are created by us because they occur according to our intentions and wills and our refraining from them if we wish. Refer to al-Tamhid... And among them is that the servant is demanded from his Lord obedience, and it is impossible in intellects that the servant be demanded what is not from him. Refer to al-Irshad... And among them is what they took from transmitted evidence such as His statement: 'And you create lies'. And the response to them is that the intended meaning is 'you fabricate lies', i.e., you make up and lie. And His statement: 'You create from clay like the shape of a bird by My permission, then you blow into it, and it becomes a bird by My permission'. And the response is that 'create' here means to determine, i.e., you determine in your heart. Refer to al-Tamhid... (1) Surah al-Ra'd, verse 16. (2) For if they say: This which you have clung to is generality, and scholars have two schools regarding general expressions: one rejecting that expressions indicate generality, and the second affirming generality while allowing interpretation; and every apparent expression is subject to probabilities, so it is not permissible to cling to it in certain matters. We say: We did not cling to mere wording until we clarified its conjunction with the intention of praise, and we showed that that praise is understood from the meaning of the verse with certainty, and it is not possible to continue carrying the verse restrictively with what we have ascertained of praise; and the understood meaning, even if not derived from mere wording, is taken from indications. For if they say: It is abandoned in its apparent meaning, for the apparent meaning requires that the Lord be the creator of everything, and the term 'thing' is applied to the eternal and the originated. We say: The addressee, the speaker in these contexts, does not fall under the judgment of the discourse, and the definitive texts are not repelled by deviations and tricks. Refer to al-Shamil...
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage presents the proof of Ahl al-Haqq (the People of Truth) from the Quranic verse 'خَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ' (He created everything). The author argues that since human actions are 'things', God is their Creator due to the generality of the verse. The Mu'tazila object by claiming that human actions are excluded because the verse is meant for praise, and including actions like slander and harm to prophets would imply blame instead of praise. They give examples of evil actions to support exclusion. The author then responds that the one who subjects himself to insult is considered foolish in the witnessed world, so how much more foolish is the one who creates such actions? After this, the passage includes a series of additional Mu'tazila doubts and responses drawn from standard references (al-Tamhid, al-Irshad, etc.), concerning creation by intention, impossibility of demanding what is not from the servant, and linguistic arguments about the term 'خلق' in other verses. Finally, a more detailed debate is presented regarding general expressions: the Mu'tazila argue that general expressions are not decisive due to possible interpretation, but the author rebuts that the generality here is strengthened by the context of praise, and that the intended meaning is certain through indications, not mere wording. The passage concludes that definitive texts cannot be repelled by tricks.

Key Terms
خلق
كل شيء
عموم
تمدن
ذم
شتم
افتراء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'خَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ' cannot include bad actions because that would imply blame for God.
Correction: The author argues that the context of praise actually requires inclusion to show God's absolute power; He creates all things, and the praise is for His power, not for the moral quality of created acts.

Checkpoint
What is the main Quranic proof used by Ahl al-Haqq to show that God creates all actions, including those of servants?
A) 'You create lies' (العنكبوت:17)
B) 'He created everything' (الرعد:16)
C) 'Allah is the creator of all things' (الزمر:62)
D) 'To Him is the creation and the command' (الأعراف:54)

Key Takeaway
The People of Truth use the generality of 'He created everything' combined with the context of praise to argue that God creates all actions, including human actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe that Allah created that action? How does that make you feel about your own responsibility? Will you use this as an excuse to continue sinning, or will it drive you to seek His forgiveness more earnestly?
?
The Mu'tazila were concerned that attributing evil actions to God would imply blame. Have you ever blamed Allah for your own wrong choices? How can the truth that Allah creates all actions, without being blameworthy, change your perspective on your own failures?
?
If Allah creates every action, including the good deeds you do, does that give you more humility or pride? How does this truth affect your gratitude for your ability to obey?

Refuting Further Doubts: Intentions, Demands, and General Expressions
Sanusi presents multiple Mu'tazila doubts and responses, and a detailed debate on general expressions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the additional Mu'tazila doubts regarding human creation of actions based on intention, divine demand, and linguistic arguments, and how the People of Truth respond, including the debate on the interpretation of general Quranic expressions.

Core Idea
Neither intentions nor demands defeat God's exclusive creation; general texts are decisive with contextual indications.

Beyond the first objection, the Mu'tazila raised further arguments: actions occur by our intention, the demand for obedience implies we create them, and other verses use the word 'create' for human actions. The People of Truth respond by clarifying the meaning of 'create' in those verses and by engaging in a detailed discussion on how general Quranic expressions are to be interpreted, emphasizing that context provides certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the additional doubts and responses
The text presents several Mu'tazila doubts, each marked by 'ومنها'. Read each doubt and its response carefully. Note how the response often reinterprets the verse in question.
The first doubt: actions are created by us because they occur according to our intentions.
2
Understand the debate on general expressions
The Mu'tazila argue that general expressions are open to interpretation and cannot be used for certain proofs. The author responds by distinguishing between mere wording and contextual indications, and asserts that the praise context makes the general meaning certain.
This is a key methodological point in kalam.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends with the assertion that definitive texts are not repelled by tricks. Consider why this matters for the overall argument.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: General Quranic expressions are always open to interpretation and cannot provide certainty.

Checkpoint
According to the author, how do the People of Truth defend the generality of the verse 'خَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ' against the Mu'tazila claim that general expressions are not decisive?
A) They rely only on the literal wording of the verse.
B) They argue that the verse's context of praise gives certainty beyond mere wording.
C) They concede that the verse is general but can be restricted by other verses.
D) They reject the Mu'tazila methodology entirely.

Key Takeaway
The definitive nature of Quranic texts is established through contextual indications, not mere wording, and cannot be overturned by speculative objections.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Mu'tazila argued that it is unjust for God to demand what He creates. Have you ever harbored resentment toward God for expecting you to obey while you struggle? How does the author's response challenge you to trust His wisdom over your limited sense of fairness?
?
This lesson shows that even authoritative texts can be twisted without context. Are there areas in your life where you have cherry-picked verses to justify your desires, ignoring the broader context? What one verse will you study in its full context this week to correct a misunderstanding?

The Verse 'Creator of All Things' Includes Human Actions
Imam Nasafi argues from the verse to include human actions in Allah's creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi uses the Qur'anic verse to argue that human actions are created by Allah, responding to three objections.

Core Idea
The verse 'Creator of all things' would lose its praise if human actions were excluded.

This passage presents Imam Nasafi's argument that the Qur'anic verse 'Allah is the Creator of all things' necessarily includes human actions. He anticipates three objections from opponents and addresses each, showing that the verse's praise of Allah would be meaningless if acts were not created by Him. We will follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
Notice the three conditional 'if' statements.
2
Identify the three objections
Find the three objections Nasafi addresses: divine wisdom, shared power, and ugliness of acts.
Each objection is introduced by 'if they say...'
3
Analyze Nasafi's responses
For each objection, note how Nasafi responds. He either references a prior answer, uses the verse itself, or makes a rational point.
4
Reflect on the argumentative strategy
Consider how Nasafi uses the verse as primary evidence and shifts the burden of proof to opponents.
This shows the kalam method of argumentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورود الآية يدل أن دخول أفعال الخلق ليس بمستحيل لأن جعل ذلك مستحيلاً يوجب التسوية بينه وبين ما دب ودرج وذا يزيل معنى التمدح الذي سيقت له الآية، على أنا نسألهم عن دليل الاستحالة فإن قالوا: دليل استحالة ذلك كون الباري حكيمًا فلا يليق به تخلیق شتم نفسه، فقد أجبنا عنه، وإن جعلوا دليل الاستحالة دخول مقدور تحت قدرة قادرين فنقول: مورد الآية يقتضي نفي الاستحالة لما في ثبوت استحالة زوال معنى التمدح على أنا نبين أن ذلك ليس بمستحيل إذا شرعنا في المعقول إن شاء الله تعالى - على أن إقامة دليل الاستحالة عليهم لا علينا، وإن جعلوا دليل الاستحالة قبح هذه الأفعال بقيت الآية حجة في ما ليس بقبيح من أفعال الخلق على أن إيجاد القبيح ليس بقبيح في المعقول، إذ تحصيل الشيء على ما ينبغي أن يكون عليه من حسن وقبح حكمة، كما أن العلم به على ما هو عليه علم وليس بجهل، ونبين حقيقة هذا الكلام إذا انتهينا إلى المعقول في المسألة - إن شاء الله.
The occurrence of the verse indicates that the inclusion of the acts of creatures is not impossible, because making that impossible necessitates equality between Him and what creeps and crawls, and that removes the meaning of praise for which the verse was brought. Moreover, we ask them for the proof of impossibility. If they say: The proof of that impossibility is that the Creator is wise, so it is not befitting for Him to create abuse of Himself, then we have already answered that. And if they make the proof of impossibility the entry of an object of power under the power of two capable beings, then we say: The context of the verse necessitates the negation of impossibility because in the establishment of impossibility there is removal of the meaning of praise, and we will show that that is not impossible when we commence on the rational (proof) if Allah wills. Moreover, establishing the proof of impossibility is upon them, not upon us. And if they make the proof of impossibility the ugliness of these acts, the verse remains a proof regarding what is not ugly among the acts of creatures, because bringing the ugly into existence is not ugly in the intellect, since bringing a thing about in the way it ought to be, whether good or bad, is wisdom, just as knowledge of it as it is knowledge and not ignorance. And we will explain the reality of this speech when we reach the rational (discussion) on the question, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument. The author (Imam Nasafi) begins by stating a key implication: the verse (referring to "Khaliq kulli shay'" – Creator of all things) indicates that including human actions in Allah's creation is not impossible, because if it were impossible, it would equate Allah with lowly creeping things, thus nullifying the praise intended by the verse. He then addresses three possible objections from opponents. First, if they argue impossibility from God's wisdom (that creating insult of Himself is unfitting), he says this has already been answered. Second, if they argue impossibility because a single act cannot fall under the power of two agents, he responds that the verse itself negates that impossibility to preserve its praise. Third, if they argue impossibility because the acts in question are ugly, he clarifies that the verse remains proof for those acts that are not ugly, and moreover, creating ugly is not itself ugly in rational terms, since achieving existence in the manner it ought to be—whether good or bad—is wisdom. He concludes by promising a fuller rational explanation later.

Key Terms
آية
خلق
فعل

Misconception: The verse 'Khaliq kulli shay'' only refers to creating bodies, not actions.
Correction: Nasafi argues that if actions were excluded, the verse's praise would be meaningless, implying actions are included.

According to Imam Nasafi, if Allah's creation of human actions were impossible, what would be the consequence regarding the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay’'?
A) It would contradict other verses.
B) It would remove the meaning of praise from the verse.
C) It would mean actions are not real.
D) It would imply two creators.

Key Takeaway
Imam Nasafi uses the Qur'anic verse to establish that the creation of human actions is not impossible, and objections based on wisdom, power, and ugliness do not refute it.

?

The Dispute Over Actions Existed Before the Prophet
Imam Nasafi refutes the historical objection by citing pre-Islamic groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Imam Nasafi refutes the claim that the dispute over creation of actions was a later innovation by citing pre-Islamic groups who held similar views.

Core Idea
The debate on divine creation of actions is ancient, not a later Muslim invention.

Imam Nasafi addresses the objection that the verse 'Creator of everything' only applies to bodies because the dispute about actions arose later. He counters by showing that similar views existed among Jews and Christians before Islam, proving the dispute is not new. Let's examine his evidence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The opponents claim the verse was only about bodies because the creation-of-actions debate wasn't around in the Prophet's time.
This is a historical-context argument.
2
Examine Nasafi's counter-claim
He asserts that the debate did exist, citing two groups.
Pay attention to the groups he mentions.
3
Analyze the evidence
Identify the 'Ananiyya Jews (similar to Mu'tazila) and most Christians (who held jabr).
Why does he mention both?
4
Conclude the refutation
Realize that Nasafi establishes that the dispute is old, thus the verse's scope is not limited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس يستقيم قولهم إن قوله تعالى: خَلَقَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ ورد في الأجسام دون الأعراض، لأن المنازعة في تخليق الأفعال ما كانت ثابتة في زمن النبي عليه السلام بل حدثت بعد ذلك، وإنما الخلاف في ذلك الزمان كان بين الموحدين وبين الثنوية والمجوس والزنادقة في تخليق الأجسام الضارة، فوردت الآية لبيان ذلك لأنا نقول: الخلاف في خلق الأفعال كان في ذلك الزمان وقبل ذلك الزمان، فإن طائفة من اليهود يقال لهم: العنانية كانوا على ما ذهبت إليه المعتزلة، وأكثر النصارى كانت تقول بالجبر، فإذا هذه دعوة كاذبة، على أنا نقول: هب أن الخلاف في هذه المسألة لم يكن في ذلك الزمان، ولكن نقول: إن الله تعالى لما كان عالما بحدوث مقالتكم الفاسدة المضاهية لأقاويل أولئك الثنوية أقام الدلالة السمعية على بطلان كل من ذلك ما كان من ذلك ثابتا وما سيحدث ما يضاهيه وهو من نتائجه، وليس بيان الكتاب بمقتصر على ما وقع في ذلك الزمان بل تضمن الكتاب بيان ذلك وبيان ما يحتاج إليه ويبتلى به إلى انقراض الدنيا وفنائها.
And their statement is not sound that the saying of the Exalted, 'Creator of everything,' was revealed concerning bodies, not accidents, because the dispute about the creation of actions was not established in the time of the Prophet, peace be upon him, but occurred after that. Rather, the disagreement in that time was between the monotheists and the dualists, Magians, and heretics concerning the creation of harmful bodies, so the verse was revealed to clarify that. For we say: The disagreement about the creation of actions existed in that time and before that time, for a group of Jews called the 'Ananiyya held what the Mu'tazila went to, and most Christians used to say jabr (compulsion). So this is a false claim. Moreover, we say: Grant that the disagreement about this matter did not exist in that time, but we say: Since Allah, the Exalted, was knowing of the occurrence of your corrupt doctrine which resembles the sayings of those dualists, He established the scriptural evidence for the falsehood of all of that—what was established of that and what would occur similar to it, which is from its consequences. And the clarification of the Book is not limited to what occurred in that time; rather, the Book includes clarification of that and clarification of what is needed and afflicted with until the end of the world and its extinction.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The opponents claim that the verse 'Khaliq kulli shay'' was revealed only about bodies, not accidents (including actions), because the dispute about the creation of human actions did not exist at the Prophet's time. Imam Nasafi refutes this in two ways. First, he argues that the dispute did exist: he cites a Jewish sect (al-'Ananiyya) that held Mu'tazilite-like views, and most Christians held the position of jabr (compulsion), implying that creation of actions was already debated. Therefore, the opponents' claim of no dispute is false. Second, even if the dispute had not existed at that time, he argues that Allah, knowing that such corrupt doctrines would arise in the future, included in the Qur'an evidence against them and against all similar doctrines, because the Book's scope extends to all times until the end of the world.

Key Terms
منازعة
زمان
ثنوية
مجوس
زنادقة
يهود
نصارى
جبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dispute about creation of actions only arose among Muslims after the Prophet's time.
Correction: Nasafi shows that similar views existed among Jews and Christians before and during the Prophet's time.

Checkpoint
Which group did Imam Nasafi cite as holding Mu'tazila-like views on the creation of actions?
A) Dualists
B) 'Ananiyya Jews
C) Magians
D) Heretics

Key Takeaway
Imam Nasafi refutes the historical objection by showing that the dispute over creation of actions predates Islam, citing the 'Ananiyya Jews and Christians.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever rejected a truth from Allah because you assumed it was a later innovation? What evidence from this lesson challenges you to examine the origins of your own beliefs more carefully? Commit to investigating at least one historical objection to a creedal point this week.
?
When someone opposes an Islamic doctrine by claiming it was 'invented later,' do you accept it without checking the evidence? How can you use the historical precedent of the 'Ananiyya Jews and Christians to respond to such objections? What will you do the next time you encounter a similar claim?
?
This lesson shows that even before Islam, groups held positions similar to the Mu'tazila and Jabriyya. Does your own stance on divine decree align more with free will or compulsion? Are you ready to defend your position with evidence from the Qur'an and reason, as Imam Nasafi did? What step will you take today to strengthen your understanding of qadar?

The Qur'an's Timeless Applicability
Imam Nasafi argues that even if the dispute was absent then, Allah's foreknowledge ensures the Qur'an refutes all future erroneous doctrines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Nasafi's second argument that even if the dispute did not exist at the time of revelation, Allah's foreknowledge ensures the Qur'an refutes all future heresies, proving its timeless scope.

Core Idea
Allah's knowledge covers all future heresies, so the Qur'an refutes them preemptively.

Even if the opponents were correct that the dispute did not exist in the Prophet's time, Imam Nasafi offers a powerful second argument: Allah, knowing all future events, included in the Qur'an refutations of doctrines that would emerge later. This shows the verse's scope transcends its immediate context.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the hypothetical scenario
Nasafi says 'Grant that the dispute did not exist at that time'.
This shows he is arguing concessively.
2
Understand Allah's foreknowledge
Because Allah knew the corrupt doctrines would arise, He placed scriptural evidence against them.
This is based on divine omniscience.
3
Recognize the universal scope of the Qur'an
The Qur'an is not limited to the Prophet's era but covers all needs until the end of the world.
This affirms the timelessness of revelation.

Exposing Contradiction: Misusing Verses to Deny Creation
Imam Nasafi criticizes opponents for inconsistent application of Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how opponents inconsistently apply Quranic verses to deny that actions are created by Allah, and the reasoning behind Imam Nasafi's refutation.

Core Idea
Inconsistent use of scripture reveals flawed reasoning, not truth.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi expresses astonishment at his opponents' shamelessness. They selectively use Quranic verses that condemn false claims about Allah's law to argue that actions are not created, while ignoring the verse that clearly affirms creation. Let's follow his critique step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source once, then the English translation. Notice the tone of astonishment and the key verses cited.
Pay attention to the words 'وقاحة' and 'تناقض'.
2
Identify the two sets of verses
The opponents use Q. 3:78 (twisting tongues) and Q. 5:103 (bahira, sa'ibah) to argue against creation of actions. Understand what each verse actually addresses.
Both verses are about declaring false religious laws, not about the nature of actions.
3
Analyze the contradiction
Imam Nasafi points out that the opponents ignore the historical context of these verses and then refuse to apply the same reasoning to the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' (Q. 37:96). They claim it refers only to bodies, not actions.
This double standard is the core of his refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعجب من وقاحتهم حيث يتعلقون في المسألة بقوله: وَإِنَّ مِنْهُمْ لَفَرِيقًا يَلْوُونَ أَلْسِنَتَهُم بِالْكِتَابِ لِتَحْسَبُوهُ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَمَا هُوَ مِنَ الْكِتَابِ وَيَقُولُونَ هُوَ مِنْ عِندِ اللَّهِ وَمَا هُوَ مِنْ عِندِ اللَّهِ وقالوا: نفى أن يكون ليهم ألسنتهم من عند الله، وكذا قوله تعالى: مَا جَعَلَ اللهُ مِنْ بَحِيرَةٍ وَلَا سَائِبَةٍ الآية، ويتعلقون به في نفي خلق الأفعال مع أن الخصوم كانوا يدعون ذلك شرعًا، والآية وردت لبيان أنها ليست بمشروعة من الله تعالى ولا يبالون من صرف الآية إلى أفعال العباد وإن لم تكن المنازعة واقعة في ذلك الزمان في تخليقها، ثم يصرفون الآية التي نتعلق بها نحن إلى غير الأفعال لانعدام المنازعة فيها في ذلك الزمان، وهذا هو عين التناقض وغاية الوقاحة والتحكم على الكتاب بآرائهم الفاسدة - عصمنا الله تعالى عن ذلك.
And astonishing is their impudence, where they cling in the matter to His saying: 'And indeed among them is a party who twist their tongues with the book that you may think it is from the book, but it is not from the book, and they say, "It is from Allah," but it is not from Allah.' And they said: He negated that their tongues are from Allah. And likewise His saying, the Exalted: 'Allah has not made bahirah, nor sa'ibah' - the verse. And they cling to it in negating the creation of actions, even though the adversaries used to claim that as law, and the verse was revealed to clarify that it is not prescribed by Allah, the Exalted. And they do not care to divert the verse to the actions of servants even though the dispute was not occurring in that time concerning their creation. Then they divert the verse by which we cling to other than actions due to the absence of dispute about it in that time. And this is the very contradiction, the utmost impudence, and arbitrary imposition on the Book with their corrupt opinions. May Allah protect us from that.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a critique of the opponents' inconsistency. The author (Imam Nasafi) expresses astonishment at their shamelessness. He points out that they use verses like the one about those who twist their tongues with the Book (Q. 3:78) and the verse about bahirah and sa'ibah (Q. 5:103) to argue that actions are not created by Allah, because these verses show that certain claims are not from Allah. However, these verses are about declaring false things as prescribed by Allah, not about the creation of actions. The opponents ignore this and apply the verses to negate creation. Then, they refuse to apply the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' to actions, claiming it was only about bodies because the dispute about actions did not exist at the time. This is a clear contradiction: they use one reasoning for the verses they like but reject the same reasoning for the verse that supports the Maturidi position. The author calls this the height of impudence and arbitrary manipulation of the Qur'an.

Key Terms
تعلق
تحريف
كتاب
بحيرة
سائبة

وقاحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Quranic verses condemning false claims (e.g., twisting tongues, banning livestock) are about the creation of human actions.
Correction: These verses address the act of declaring false religious laws, not the ontological question of whether actions are created by Allah. The opponents ignore the context.

Checkpoint
What does Imam Nasafi identify as the core contradiction in the opponents' argument?
A) They use verses about false religious laws to deny creation of actions, but refuse to apply a clear verse about creation to actions.
B) They believe in free will.
C) They are Jews.
D) They deny all verses.

Key Takeaway
The opponents' selective application of Quranic verses exposes their arbitrary methodology and is a clear contradiction.

?

Proof from the Verse 'Allah Created You and What You Do'
Imam Nasafi cites Quran 37:96 as proof for creation of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi uses the Qur'anic verse (37:96) as a direct textual proof for the Maturidi doctrine that Allah creates human actions.

Core Idea
The verse 'Allah created you and what you do' explicitly attributes the creation of actions to Allah.

Imam Nasafi now brings a decisive Qur'anic proof. The verse from Surah As-Saffat explicitly states that Allah creates both humans and their actions. This concise testimony leaves no room for alternative interpretations that would deny divine creation of deeds. Let us examine the verse and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its context
Read the Arabic text of the verse and its literal translation. Notice that the phrase 'wa ma ta'malun' is general—it encompasses all actions, not just objects.
The verse is from Surah As-Saffat 37:96.
2
Understand how it proves the doctrine
Reflect on why this verse is considered a direct proof. It attributes creation to both humans and their actions using the same verb 'khalaqa', indicating that actions are created entities.
The Maturidi position is that Allah creates the action; humans acquire it.
3
Consider the alternative interpretation
Some argue that 'ma ta'malun' means 'what you make' (i.e., crafted objects). Evaluate whether the verse's generality supports that limitation.
The common misunderstanding is addressed below.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يدل على صحة ما ذهبنا إليه قوله تعالى: وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ
And among what indicates the correctness of what we have gone to is His statement, may He be Exalted: 'And Allah created you and what you do.'
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a simple proof. The author (Imam Nasafi) cites a Quranic verse (Surah As-Saffat 37:96) as direct evidence for the Maturidi position that Allah creates human actions. The verse states: 'And Allah created you and what you do.' It clearly attributes both the creation of humans and their actions to Allah, leaving no room for the claim that actions are not created by Him. This is a straightforward textual proof for the doctrine of khalq al-af'al (creation of actions).

Key Terms
خلق
فعل
دليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'ma ta'malun' refers only to objects made by human hands (e.g., carvings), not to actions like walking or thinking.
Correction: The word 'ma' is a general relative pronoun; it encompasses all that one does, including actions. The context of the verse (addressing idolaters who carved idols) does not restrict its meaning to crafted objects only.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does Imam Nasafi use as a final proof for the creation of human actions?
A) Surah Al-Imran (3:78)
B) Surah Al-Ma'idah (5:103)
C) Surah As-Saffat (37:96)
D) Surah Al-Fatihah (1:1)

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse 'Allah created you and what you do' directly proves that Allah is the Creator of human actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah creates even your smallest actions, do you truly acknowledge that every good deed is from Him? How does that change the way you express gratitude?
?
When you sin, do you feel that Allah created that action? How does that affect your repentance and your view of His justice and mercy?
?
This verse removes any claim of independent power from you. Are you willing to accept that you are not the ultimate originator of your actions? How will that transform your reliance on Allah?

The Grammatical Rule: 'Ma' with Verb Means the Action
Al-Nasafi states the grammatical rule and the opponent's objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the grammatical rule that when 'ma' is attached to a verb without a pronoun, it denotes the verbal noun (action), according to Sibawayh, and the objection raised by the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
When 'ma' meets a verb without a pronoun, it points to the action, not the object.

Al-Nasafi begins by stating the Maturidi position that 'ma ta'malun' in the Quran refers to the act of doing, not the thing done. He grounds this in a grammatical principle from the renowned grammarian Sibawayh. The Mu'tazila object, claiming the verse means the objects (idols). This lesson unpacks the grammatical argument that forms the foundation of the debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the grammatical passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully to understand the rule and the objection. Note the example 'a'jabani ma sana'ta'.
The example shows the difference between action and object.
2
Identify the rule and exception
Find the rule: 'ma' with verb = masdar (action) when no pronoun (ha) is present. Also find the exception: with the pronoun, it denotes the object.
Sibawayh's position is the standard grammatical rule.
3
Understand the opponents' objection
The Mu'tazila object by citing verses like 'Do you worship what you carve?' – they claim the verse refers to the carved objects, not the action of carving.
This sets up the need for additional evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي وعملكم فإن كلمة ما إذا اتصلت بالفعل صارا عبارة عن المصدر تقول: أعجبني ما صنعت أي صنعك، والخصوم يعترضون على هذا ويقولون: المراد منه المعمول أي خلقكم ومعمولكم وهي الأصنام المعمولة وهي أجسام ولا خلاف في كونها مخلوقة نظيره قوله تعالى: أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ وهم ما كانوا يعبدون فعلهم الذي هو النحت بل كانوا يعبدون المنحوت، وكذا قوله: تَلْقَفُ مَا يَأْفِكُونَ . والجواب أن كلمة ما إذا اتصلت بالفعل كان مجموعها عبارة عن المصدر عند الإطلاق هذا هو مذهب سيبويه وإن خالفه الأخفش في ذلك حيث جوز سيبويه أن يقال أعجبني ما قمت أي قيامك، ولو كان ذا عبارة عن المفعول لما جاز ذلك إلا في الفعل المتعدي، والأخفش لا يجوزه إلا في المعتدي، غير أن العارفين بكلام العرب المتبحرين في علم النحو مالوا إلى تصحيح قول سيبوبه، وإذا ذكر العائد وهو الهاء فقيل: أعجبني ما صنعته حينئذ تكون عبارة عن المفعول، وفي كل موضع جعل عبارة عن المفعول كان بإضمار الهاء وهو عدول عن ظاهر الكلام بالدليل ولا دليل فمن ادعى قيام الدليل فليبرزوه، والدليل على أنه عند الإطلاق ينصرف إلى ما بينا قوله تعالى: جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ أي بعملهم دون معمولهم، وقال تعالى: ادْخُلُوا الْجَنَّةَ بِمَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ أي بعملكم إذ الجزاء يكون بالعمل دون المعمول، وكذا دخول الجنة، وكذا في قوله تعالى: أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنحِتُونَ أي نحتكم لأنهم لما كانوا لا يعبدون تلك الأعيان إلا بعدما نحتوا ولم يروها مستحقة للعبادة إلا به صاروا في الحقيقة عابدين نحتهم دون منحوتهم ومما يتعجب منه العاقل أن المعتزلة يتعلقون في المسألة بقوله تعالى: مَا جَعَلَ اللَّهُ مِن بَحِيرَةٍ والآية، ويصرفون ذلك إلى فعلهم في هذه الأعيان، ولا شك أن المذكور في الآية أعيان لا أفعال، ثم إذا آل الأمر إلى هذا الذي هو اسم الفعل صرفوه إلى محل الفعل وبمثل هذا يتبين أنهم يلعبون بكتاب الله ويحملونه على ما تميل إليه أهواؤهم دون ما توجبه حقائق الأدلة، على أنا وإن صرفنا الآية إلى المعمول، وجعلنا كأنه قال: والله خلقكم ومعمولكم فالاستدلال بالآية باق لأن الله تعالى لم يكن خالقا للمعمول لو لم يكن عملهم مخلوقا له لأن ذلك الجسم بدون عمل العباد لا وهو تعالى أثبت الخلق للمعمول فدل أن العمل الذي صار به الجسم يكون معموالا.
Meaning: 'and your work' – indeed the word 'ma' when attached to a verb becomes an expression for the verbal noun (masdar). You say: 'I liked what you did' i.e., your doing. And the opponents object to this and say: What is meant by it is the object, i.e., 'He created you and your objects' – and they are the made idols, which are bodies, and there is no dispute about their being created. The like of that is His saying: 'Do you worship what you carve?' – and they were not worshipping their action, which is carving, but rather they were worshipping the carved object; and likewise His saying: 'It swallows what they faked.' The answer: The word 'ma' when attached to the verb, the whole of it is an expression for the verbal noun (masdar) when unrestricted – this is the doctrine of Sibawayh, even though al-Akhfash disagreed with him in that. For Sibawayh allowed that one say 'I liked what you stood' i.e., your standing; and if it were an expression for the object, that would only be permissible with transitive verbs. And al-Akhfash only allows it with transitive verbs. However, those knowledgeable in the speech of the Arabs, well-versed in grammar, have inclined to correct Sibawayh's statement. And when the referent (the pronoun 'ha') is mentioned, so it is said: 'I liked what you made it' – then it becomes an expression for the object. And every place where it is made an expression for the object, it is by implying the pronoun 'ha', and that is a deviation from the apparent meaning of speech by evidence, and there is no evidence. So whoever claims that evidence exists, let them produce it. And the proof that it, when unrestricted, refers to what we mentioned is His saying: 'A reward for what they used to do' i.e., for their action, not their object; and His saying: 'Enter Paradise for what you used to do' i.e., for your action, because recompense is for action, not for the object; and likewise entering Paradise; and likewise in His saying: 'Do you worship what you carve?' i.e., your carving, because since they did not worship those entities except after they carved them and did not consider them deserving of worship except by that, they became in reality worshippers of their carving, not their carved object. And among things that the rational person marvels at is that the Mu'tazila rely in this matter on His saying: 'Allah has not made a bahirah' and the verse, and they turn that to their action in these entities. And there is no doubt that what is mentioned in the verse is entities, not actions. Then, when the matter comes to this which is the noun of action, they turn it to the locus of action. And by this it becomes clear that they play with the Book of Allah and interpret it according to their whims, not according to the realities of evidence. However, even if we interpret the verse as referring to the object, and make it as if He said: 'Allah created you and your object', the istidlal (deduction) by the verse remains, because Allah would not be the Creator of the object if their action were not created by Him, because that body without the action of the servants is not [complete?]. And He, exalted, established creation for the object, so it indicates that the action by which the body becomes an object is [created].
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection regarding the interpretation of 'ma ta'malun' (what you do) in the Qur'an. The opponents (likely Mu'tazila) argue that it refers to the object (the idols made by human hands), not the action (the act of making). Al-Nasafi begins by stating the Maturidi position: when 'ma' is attached to a verb, the combination expresses the masdar (verbal noun), i.e., the action. He gives an example: 'a'jabani ma sana'ta' means 'I liked your doing', not 'I liked what you made'. The opponents counter that it means the object, citing verses like 'Do you worship what you carve?' (al-Saffat 37:95) – they say the polytheists worshipped the carved objects, not the act of carving. Al-Nasafi responds with a grammatical argument. He invokes the authority of Sibawayh, who holds that 'ma' with a verb always denotes the masdar when no object pronoun (ha') is present. If a pronoun is added (e.g., 'ma sana'tahu'), then it denotes the object. The opponents' reading would require an implied pronoun, which is a deviation from the apparent meaning and lacks evidence. Al-Nasafi then provides Qur'anic support: verses like 'Jaza'an bima kanu ya'malun' (reward for what they used to do) and 'udkhulu al-jannata bima kuntum ta'malun' clearly refer to actions, not objects, because reward is for deeds. Similarly, 'ata'buduna ma tanhitun' means 'do you worship your carving?' because the act of carving is what made the idols worthy of worship in their eyes. Al-Nasafi then criticizes the Mu'tazila for inconsistency: in the verse about bahirah (a type of camel), they interpret 'ma ja'ala Allahu min bahirah' as referring to the act of prohibition, not the animal, yet in the verse under discussion they insist on the object. This shows they manipulate the text to suit their views. Finally, he argues that even if 'ma ta'malun' is taken as the object, the conclusion still holds: the object (idol) is created by Allah only if the human action that makes it is also created by Allah. Thus, the verse still proves that human actions are created by Allah.

Key Terms
ما
مصدر
مفعول
سيبويه
الأخفش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'ma ta'malun' always refers to the physical objects produced by human action.
Correction: Grammatically, when 'ma' is attached to a verb without a pronoun, it denotes the action (masdar), not the object. The object reading requires an implied pronoun, which is a deviation from the apparent meaning.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the grammatical rule of 'ma' when attached to a verb without the pronoun?
A) It denotes the object (maf'ul) of the verb
B) It denotes the verbal noun (masdar) of the verb
C) It can denote either the action or the object equally
D) It denotes the doer of the action

Key Takeaway
The default meaning of 'ma' with a verb is the action, not the object, unless the pronoun 'ha' is attached.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quranic verse 'أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ', do you naturally assume it refers to the carved idols? This lesson shows that grammar points to the act of carving. How does this careful attention to language challenge your usual reading habits? Will you commit to studying Arabic grammar more deeply to avoid misinterpreting Allah's words?
?
The opponents here misinterpreted 'ma ta'malun' to support their theological agenda. Have you ever twisted a text to fit your own desires? In what area of your life do you need to submit to the precise meaning of divine revelation, even when it is uncomfortable? What is one step you will take this week to correct such a misinterpretation?
?
Sibawayh's rule is accepted by the majority of grammarians. Do you rely on the consensus of scholars in matters of faith, or do you follow your own opinion? How does this lesson expose a need for humility and trust in those who are well-versed in the Speech of Allah? What will you change in your approach to learning?

Qur'anic Evidence: Actions, Not Objects
Al-Nasafi provides Qur'anic proof for the action interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses Qur'anic verses to prove that 'ma ta'malun' and similar expressions refer to actions, not objects, and why the opponents' interpretation fails.

Core Idea
Qur'anic verses confirm that recompense and worship are linked to actions, not objects.

After establishing the grammatical rule, Al-Nasafi turns to the Quran to provide concrete evidence. He cites verses where the word 'ma' with a verb clearly means the action, such as in the context of reward and entering Paradise. This lesson explores those verses and the reasoning that supports the Maturidi interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof verses
Read the Arabic passage containing the Qur'anic verses. Note each verse and how Al-Nasafi uses it as evidence.
The verses are about reward (jaza') and entering Paradise.
2
Analyze the logic
Understand why recompense is for actions, not objects. This is a rational principle that supports the grammatical rule.
The principle is that reward and punishment are based on deeds.
3
Examine the 'carving' verse
Look at the verse 'Do you worship what you carve?' and see how Al-Nasafi argues that it means worshipping the carving action, not the carved object.
The polytheists' worship depended on the act of carving.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your entrance to Paradise depends on your actions, not the objects you produce or own, how does that change what you prioritize each day? Will you today shift focus from accumulating things to performing sincere deeds?
?
The polytheists worshipped their own act of carving. Are there any acts of worship in your life that have become mechanical, where you are more focused on the ritual itself than on the One you claim to worship? What will you do about it before your next prayer?
?
You know that reward is based on deeds, not the 'things' you consider achievements. Is your sense of self-worth tied to what you have done (actions) or to what you have accumulated (objects)? Write down one action you can take today purely for Allah, with no worldly return.

Refutation of Mu'tazila: Inconsistency and Final Argument
Al-Nasafi critiques Mu'tazila and provides a final argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Nasafi's critique of the Mu'tazila's inconsistent interpretation of Quranic verses and his final argument that even if 'ma ta'malun' is taken as the object, it still proves that human actions are created by Allah.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila play with Allah's Book, twisting verses to fit their whims.

Al-Nasafi concludes his argument by exposing a contradiction in the Mu'tazilite approach. In one verse they interpret 'ma' as the action, but in this verse they insist on the object. He then provides a final, powerful argument: even if the verse refers to the object (the idols), that still proves that human actions are created by Allah, because the object is only made possible by the action. This lesson examines the critique and the deeper theological point.

Guided Path
1
Read the critique of Mu'tazila
Read the part where Al-Nasafi points out the Mu'tazila's inconsistency: they interpret 'ma' in the bahirah verse as the action, but here as the object.
This is a charge of hypocrisy in methodology.
2
Understand the final argument
Even if we accept the object reading, the verse still proves that actions are created. Why? Because the object (idol) is created by Allah only if the human action that makes it an object is also created.
This is a conditional argument linking creation of object to creation of action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي وعملكم فإن كلمة ما إذا اتصلت بالفعل صارا عبارة عن المصدر تقول: أعجبني ما صنعت أي صنعك، والخصوم يعترضون على هذا ويقولون: المراد منه المعمول أي خلقكم ومعمولكم وهي الأصنام المعمولة وهي أجسام ولا خلاف في كونها مخلوقة نظيره قوله تعالى: أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ وهم ما كانوا يعبدون فعلهم الذي هو النحت بل كانوا يعبدون المنحوت، وكذا قوله: تَلْقَفُ مَا يَأْفِكُونَ . والجواب أن كلمة ما إذا اتصلت بالفعل كان مجموعها عبارة عن المصدر عند الإطلاق هذا هو مذهب سيبويه وإن خالفه الأخفش في ذلك حيث جوز سيبويه أن يقال أعجبني ما قمت أي قيامك، ولو كان ذا عبارة عن المفعول لما جاز ذلك إلا في الفعل المتعدي، والأخفش لا يجوزه إلا في المعتدي، غير أن العارفين بكلام العرب المتبحرين في علم النحو مالوا إلى تصحيح قول سيبوبه، وإذا ذكر العائد وهو الهاء فقيل: أعجبني ما صنعته حينئذ تكون عبارة عن المفعول، وفي كل موضع جعل عبارة عن المفعول كان بإضمار الهاء وهو عدول عن ظاهر الكلام بالدليل ولا دليل فمن ادعى قيام الدليل فليبرزوه، والدليل على أنه عند الإطلاق ينصرف إلى ما بينا قوله تعالى: جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ أي بعملهم دون معمولهم، وقال تعالى: ادْخُلُوا الْجَنَّةَ بِمَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ أي بعملكم إذ الجزاء يكون بالعمل دون المعمول، وكذا دخول الجنة، وكذا في قوله تعالى: أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنحِتُونَ أي نحتكم لأنهم لما كانوا لا يعبدون تلك الأعيان إلا بعدما نحتوا ولم يروها مستحقة للعبادة إلا به صاروا في الحقيقة عابدين نحتهم دون منحوتهم ومما يتعجب منه العاقل أن المعتزلة يتعلقون في المسألة بقوله تعالى: مَا جَعَلَ اللَّهُ مِن بَحِيرَةٍ والآية، ويصرفون ذلك إلى فعلهم في هذه الأعيان، ولا شك أن المذكور في الآية أعيان لا أفعال، ثم إذا آل الأمر إلى هذا الذي هو اسم الفعل صرفوه إلى محل الفعل وبمثل هذا يتبين أنهم يلعبون بكتاب الله ويحملونه على ما تميل إليه أهواؤهم دون ما توجبه حقائق الأدلة، على أنا وإن صرفنا الآية إلى المعمول، وجعلنا كأنه قال: والله خلقكم ومعمولكم فالاستدلال بالآية باق لأن الله تعالى لم يكن خالقا للمعمول لو لم يكن عملهم مخلوقا له لأن ذلك الجسم بدون عمل العباد لا وهو تعالى أثبت الخلق للمعمول فدل أن العمل الذي صار به الجسم يكون معموالا.
Meaning: 'and your work' – indeed the word 'ma' when attached to a verb becomes an expression for the verbal noun (masdar). You say: 'I liked what you did' i.e., your doing. And the opponents object to this and say: What is meant by it is the object, i.e., 'He created you and your objects' – and they are the made idols, which are bodies, and there is no dispute about their being created. The like of that is His saying: 'Do you worship what you carve?' – and they were not worshipping their action, which is carving, but rather they were worshipping the carved object; and likewise His saying: 'It swallows what they faked.' The answer: The word 'ma' when attached to the verb, the whole of it is an expression for the verbal noun (masdar) when unrestricted – this is the doctrine of Sibawayh, even though al-Akhfash disagreed with him in that. For Sibawayh allowed that one say 'I liked what you stood' i.e., your standing; and if it were an expression for the object, that would only be permissible with transitive verbs. And al-Akhfash only allows it with transitive verbs. However, those knowledgeable in the speech of the Arabs, well-versed in grammar, have inclined to correct Sibawayh's statement. And when the referent (the pronoun 'ha') is mentioned, so it is said: 'I liked what you made it' – then it becomes an expression for the object. And every place where it is made an expression for the object, it is by implying the pronoun 'ha', and that is a deviation from the apparent meaning of speech by evidence, and there is no evidence. So whoever claims that evidence exists, let them produce it. And the proof that it, when unrestricted, refers to what we mentioned is His saying: 'A reward for what they used to do' i.e., for their action, not their object; and His saying: 'Enter Paradise for what you used to do' i.e., for your action, because recompense is for action, not for the object; and likewise entering Paradise; and likewise in His saying: 'Do you worship what you carve?' i.e., your carving, because since they did not worship those entities except after they carved them and did not consider them deserving of worship except by that, they became in reality worshippers of their carving, not their carved object. And among things that the rational person marvels at is that the Mu'tazila rely in this matter on His saying: 'Allah has not made a bahirah' and the verse, and they turn that to their action in these entities. And there is no doubt that what is mentioned in the verse is entities, not actions. Then, when the matter comes to this which is the noun of action, they turn it to the locus of action. And by this it becomes clear that they play with the Book of Allah and interpret it according to their whims, not according to the realities of evidence. However, even if we interpret the verse as referring to the object, and make it as if He said: 'Allah created you and your object', the istidlal (deduction) by the verse remains, because Allah would not be the Creator of the object if their action were not created by Him, because that body without the action of the servants is not [complete?]. And He, exalted, established creation for the object, so it indicates that the action by which the body becomes an object is [created].
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection regarding the interpretation of 'ma ta'malun' (what you do) in the Qur'an. The opponents (likely Mu'tazila) argue that it refers to the object (the idols made by human hands), not the action (the act of making). Al-Nasafi begins by stating the Maturidi position: when 'ma' is attached to a verb, the combination expresses the masdar (verbal noun), i.e., the action. He gives an example: 'a'jabani ma sana'ta' means 'I liked your doing', not 'I liked what you made'. The opponents counter that it means the object, citing verses like 'Do you worship what you carve?' (al-Saffat 37:95) – they say the polytheists worshipped the carved objects, not the act of carving. Al-Nasafi responds with a grammatical argument. He invokes the authority of Sibawayh, who holds that 'ma' with a verb always denotes the masdar when no object pronoun (ha') is present. If a pronoun is added (e.g., 'ma sana'tahu'), then it denotes the object. The opponents' reading would require an implied pronoun, which is a deviation from the apparent meaning and lacks evidence. Al-Nasafi then provides Qur'anic support: verses like 'Jaza'an bima kanu ya'malun' (reward for what they used to do) and 'udkhulu al-jannata bima kuntum ta'malun' clearly refer to actions, not objects, because reward is for deeds. Similarly, 'ata'buduna ma tanhitun' means 'do you worship your carving?' because the act of carving is what made the idols worthy of worship in their eyes. Al-Nasafi then criticizes the Mu'tazila for inconsistency: in the verse about bahirah (a type of camel), they interpret 'ma ja'ala Allahu min bahirah' as referring to the act of prohibition, not the animal, yet in the verse under discussion they insist on the object. This shows they manipulate the text to suit their views. Finally, he argues that even if 'ma ta'malun' is taken as the object, the conclusion still holds: the object (idol) is created by Allah only if the human action that makes it is also created by Allah. Thus, the verse still proves that human actions are created by Allah.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
بحيرة
خلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Mu'tazila are consistent in their interpretation of 'ma' across all verses.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows they inconsistently interpret 'ma' as action in some verses and as object in others, revealing their bias.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Nasafi's final argument, even if 'ma ta'malun' means the object, what does it still prove?
A) That idols are not created by Allah
B) That human actions are created by Allah
C) That the object is not real
D) That the verse is unclear

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's inconsistency reveals their subjective interpretation, but even their own reading of the verse confirms that actions are created by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever twisted a verse of the Quran to justify a desire or habit you were unwilling to give up? What would it take for you to submit to the plain meaning even when it is uncomfortable?
?
If your actions are truly created by Allah, what does that mean for your sense of pride or self-reliance? Are you willing to see every deed—good or bad—as coming from Him?
?
When you read the Quran, do you seek the truth even when it challenges your beliefs, or do you unconsciously look for support for what you already think? Will you pray for Allah to guide you to His intended meaning?

Direct Textual Proof from Quran 67:13-14
Al-Nasafi presents the direct textual proof from the verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi uses Quran 67:13-14 as a direct textual proof that Allah creates human actions.

Core Idea
The verse directly links knowledge to creation, implying actions are created.

Al-Nasafi begins by citing the verse and then explains why it is a clear, direct proof. He argues that the verse does not merely state Allah’s knowledge but uses that knowledge to affirm that He is the Creator of the actions He knows. This lesson examines the direct textual argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how al-Nasafi first cites the verse and then unpacks its implication.
Pay attention to the phrase 'أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ' which is the key.
2
Identify the direct proof structure
Al-Nasafi explains that the verse states Allah's knowledge of concealed and public speech, then asks 'Does He who created not know?' This creates a link: since Allah knows the actions, they must be created by Him. Identify this reasoning in the text.
3
Reflect on the clarity of the proof
Consider why al-Nasafi calls this 'among the clearest proofs from the texts.' How does the verse leave no room for doubt that Allah creates actions?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الكتاب فقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَأَسِرُّوا قَوْلَكُمْ أَوِ اجْهَرُوا بِهِ إِنَّهُ عَلِيمٌ بِذَاتِ الصُّدُورِ أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وَهُوَ اللَّطِيفُ الْخَبِيرُ ﴾ فالآية تنص على أنه خالق أفعال العباد، وفيها أيضًا إشارة إلى أن كل خالق ينبغي أن يكون عالمًا بما خلق، أما كونها نصا فظاهر فإنه تعالى أخبر أنه يعلم ما يسر به العبد في قلبه وما يجهر به وقال : أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ ) وهو بيان أنه هو الخالق لأنه جعل كونه خالقًا مقررا لما أخبر من تعلق علمه به كأنه قال: وهل يتصور أن لا يعلم من خلقه وأبدا ثبته بما هو أظهر منه ولا يرتاب أحد في كون الأفعال معلومة لله تعالى والله تعالى جعل العلم بهذا ثابتاً بثبوت تخليقه له، فكان هذا إخباراً بكونه مخلوقا له ثم بنى لثبوت العلم به على كونه مخلوقا له، ومثل هذا من أظهر ما يستدل به من النصوص. وأما الإشارة فلأنه أثبت علمه بما أسروا أو جهروا بإثبات تخليقه لذلك، ولو جاز التخليق ممن لا علم له بما خلق لم يكن إثبات العلم بإثبات ما يجوز ثبوته بدون العلم حكمة، كمن يقول لآخر : أنا عالم بالفقه والكلام ثم يقول : ألا أعلم أنا ذلك وأنا ابن بزاز؟ أو يقول: وأنا طويل أو قصير أو وأنا عراقي أو حجازي أو يقول: ألا يعلم الفقه ممن هو بطل كمي أو جواد سخي؟ جل الله تعالى أن يثبت علمه بشيء بناء على ما لا يوجب له العلم به، ويجوز تعريه عن العلم فيكون في إثباته سفها مثبتًا الشيء بما لا يجب ثبوته به كالذين يجهلون طرق إثبات الأشياء على منكري ثبوتها، فصح ما ادعينا من ثبوت العلم بالمخلوق شرطًا لثبوت قدرة التخليق أو قرينة لها لا يزيلها بوجه من الوجوه في حال من الأحوال مع ما كانت الآية نصا، في إثبات خلق أفعال العباد، فإذا أثبت الله تعالى قول أهل الحق لكتابه نصا وأشار لهم أيضا إلى ما هو المعقول في المسألة نصرة من الله تعالى لحزبه وتأييدًا لدينه بكلا نوعي الحجة أعني بهما السمعي والعقلي، والله تعالى يحق الحق ويبطل الباطل ولو كره المجرمون.
As for the Book (Qur'an), His statement: 'Conceal your speech or declare it; indeed He is Knower of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Aware?' (67:13-14). The verse states that He is the Creator of the actions of the servants. In it also is an indication that every creator should know what he creates. As for its being a direct text, it is apparent: He informed that He knows what the servant conceals in his heart and what he declares, and He said: 'Does He who created not know?' This is a statement that He is the Creator because He made His being a Creator a confirmation of what He informed of the attachment of His knowledge to it, as if He said: Is it conceivable that He does not know who created? And He established it by what is more apparent, and no one doubts that actions are known to Allah. Allah made knowledge of this established by the establishment of His creation of it, so this was an indication that it is created by Him, then He built the establishment of knowledge of it upon its being created by Him. This is among the clearest proofs from the texts. As for the indication: He established His knowledge of what they conceal or declare by establishing His creation of that. If creation were permissible from one who has no knowledge of what he creates, then establishing knowledge by establishing what is possible to exist without knowledge would not be wisdom. Like one who says to another: I am knowledgeable in jurisprudence and theology, then says: Do I not know that while I am the son of a cloth merchant? Or says: I am tall or short, or I am Iraqi or Hijazi, or says: Does he who is a brave hero or a generous giver not know jurisprudence? Far be it from Allah that He should establish His knowledge of something based on what does not necessitate knowledge of it, and it is permissible for it to be devoid of knowledge, for that would be foolishness in establishing something by what does not necessitate its existence, like those who are ignorant of ways to establish things against those who deny them. So what we claimed is correct: that the establishment of knowledge of the created is a condition for the establishment of the power of creation or an indicator thereof that is not removed by any means in any circumstance, especially since the verse is a direct text in establishing the creation of the actions of the servants. Thus, Allah established the statement of the people of truth as a direct text in His Book and also indicated to them what is rational in the matter, as a victory from Allah for His party and support for His religion with both types of proof, i.e., scriptural and rational. And Allah establishes the truth and abolishes falsehood, even if the criminals dislike it.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents the proof from Quran 67:13-14 that Allah creates human actions. The author, al-Nasafi, first cites the verse and then explains two aspects: the direct textual proof (نص) and the rational indication (إشارة). The direct proof is that the verse explicitly states that Allah knows what is hidden and declared, and then asks 'Does He who created not know?' This links knowledge to creation, implying that the actions known are also created by Him. The author argues that if Allah's knowledge of actions is used to confirm that He is their Creator, then the knowledge must be based on creation, making the actions created by Him. The indication is that the verse establishes Allah's knowledge of speech (concealed or public) by establishing His creation of that speech. If creation were possible without knowledge, then using creation to prove knowledge would be meaningless and foolish, like a person claiming knowledge of something based on an irrelevant personal attribute. Therefore, the creation of actions is a necessary condition for Allah's knowledge of them, and the verse proves both. The passage concludes that Allah has provided both scriptural and rational proof for this doctrine.

Key Terms
نص (direct text)
خلق أفعال العباد (creation of human actions)
علم (knowledge)
خالق (Creator)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse only proves Allah's knowledge, not that He creates actions.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that the verse uses knowledge to imply creation, making it a direct proof of creation.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, what does the phrase 'أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ' in the verse primarily indicate?
A) That Allah knows everything
B) That Allah is the Creator of human actions
C) That Allah is Latif and Khabir
D) That humans create their own actions

Key Takeaway
The verse directly proves that Allah creates human actions by linking His knowledge of actions to His being their Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah truly knows even the thoughts you conceal and has created them, what does that mean for the way you think about your private moments? Will you now treat your inner world with more awareness of His presence?
?
When you commit a sin, do you tend to blame your circumstances or yourself? How does knowing that Allah created that action shape the sincerity of your repentance and your reliance on Him to change?
?
The verse shows that Allah's knowledge is not passive but intimately tied to His creative power. In what area of your life do you need to stop treating Allah's knowledge as mere information and start treating it as a call to turn to the Creator for change?

Rational Indication from Quran 67:13-14
Al-Nasafi presents the rational indication from the same verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's rational argument from the verse that creation necessarily implies knowledge, and why this refutes objections.

Core Idea
If creation were possible without knowledge, using it to prove knowledge would be absurd.

Al-Nasafi presents a second layer of proof from the same verse: a rational indication that the Creator must know what He creates. He uses an analogy to show that the verse’s structure would be meaningless unless Allah actually creates the actions He knows. This lesson explores that rational argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the indication passage
Read the Arabic for the indication part and its translation. Notice how al-Nasafi explains that the verse establishes knowledge of actions by establishing creation.
2
Understand the rational argument
Al-Nasafi argues that if creation could occur without knowledge, then using creation to prove knowledge would be like a person claiming knowledge of jurisprudence based on being a cloth merchant's son. This would be foolish. Identify the analogy and its point.
3
Grasp the conclusion
Al-Nasafi concludes that knowledge of the created is a condition for the power of creation. Thus, the verse rationally proves that Allah creates actions. Reflect on how this strengthens the textual proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الكتاب فقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَأَسِرُّوا قَوْلَكُمْ أَوِ اجْهَرُوا بِهِ إِنَّهُ عَلِيمٌ بِذَاتِ الصُّدُورِ أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وَهُوَ اللَّطِيفُ الْخَبِيرُ ﴾ فالآية تنص على أنه خالق أفعال العباد، وفيها أيضًا إشارة إلى أن كل خالق ينبغي أن يكون عالمًا بما خلق، أما كونها نصا فظاهر فإنه تعالى أخبر أنه يعلم ما يسر به العبد في قلبه وما يجهر به وقال : أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ ) وهو بيان أنه هو الخالق لأنه جعل كونه خالقًا مقررا لما أخبر من تعلق علمه به كأنه قال: وهل يتصور أن لا يعلم من خلقه وأبدا ثبته بما هو أظهر منه ولا يرتاب أحد في كون الأفعال معلومة لله تعالى والله تعالى جعل العلم بهذا ثابتاً بثبوت تخليقه له، فكان هذا إخباراً بكونه مخلوقا له ثم بنى لثبوت العلم به على كونه مخلوقا له، ومثل هذا من أظهر ما يستدل به من النصوص. وأما الإشارة فلأنه أثبت علمه بما أسروا أو جهروا بإثبات تخليقه لذلك، ولو جاز التخليق ممن لا علم له بما خلق لم يكن إثبات العلم بإثبات ما يجوز ثبوته بدون العلم حكمة، كمن يقول لآخر : أنا عالم بالفقه والكلام ثم يقول : ألا أعلم أنا ذلك وأنا ابن بزاز؟ أو يقول: وأنا طويل أو قصير أو وأنا عراقي أو حجازي أو يقول: ألا يعلم الفقه ممن هو بطل كمي أو جواد سخي؟ جل الله تعالى أن يثبت علمه بشيء بناء على ما لا يوجب له العلم به، ويجوز تعريه عن العلم فيكون في إثباته سفها مثبتًا الشيء بما لا يجب ثبوته به كالذين يجهلون طرق إثبات الأشياء على منكري ثبوتها، فصح ما ادعينا من ثبوت العلم بالمخلوق شرطًا لثبوت قدرة التخليق أو قرينة لها لا يزيلها بوجه من الوجوه في حال من الأحوال مع ما كانت الآية نصا، في إثبات خلق أفعال العباد، فإذا أثبت الله تعالى قول أهل الحق لكتابه نصا وأشار لهم أيضا إلى ما هو المعقول في المسألة نصرة من الله تعالى لحزبه وتأييدًا لدينه بكلا نوعي الحجة أعني بهما السمعي والعقلي، والله تعالى يحق الحق ويبطل الباطل ولو كره المجرمون.
As for the Book (Qur'an), His statement: 'Conceal your speech or declare it; indeed He is Knower of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Aware?' (67:13-14). The verse states that He is the Creator of the actions of the servants. In it also is an indication that every creator should know what he creates. As for its being a direct text, it is apparent: He informed that He knows what the servant conceals in his heart and what he declares, and He said: 'Does He who created not know?' This is a statement that He is the Creator because He made His being a Creator a confirmation of what He informed of the attachment of His knowledge to it, as if He said: Is it conceivable that He does not know who created? And He established it by what is more apparent, and no one doubts that actions are known to Allah. Allah made knowledge of this established by the establishment of His creation of it, so this was an indication that it is created by Him, then He built the establishment of knowledge of it upon its being created by Him. This is among the clearest proofs from the texts. As for the indication: He established His knowledge of what they conceal or declare by establishing His creation of that. If creation were permissible from one who has no knowledge of what he creates, then establishing knowledge by establishing what is possible to exist without knowledge would not be wisdom. Like one who says to another: I am knowledgeable in jurisprudence and theology, then says: Do I not know that while I am the son of a cloth merchant? Or says: I am tall or short, or I am Iraqi or Hijazi, or says: Does he who is a brave hero or a generous giver not know jurisprudence? Far be it from Allah that He should establish His knowledge of something based on what does not necessitate knowledge of it, and it is permissible for it to be devoid of knowledge, for that would be foolishness in establishing something by what does not necessitate its existence, like those who are ignorant of ways to establish things against those who deny them. So what we claimed is correct: that the establishment of knowledge of the created is a condition for the establishment of the power of creation or an indicator thereof that is not removed by any means in any circumstance, especially since the verse is a direct text in establishing the creation of the actions of the servants. Thus, Allah established the statement of the people of truth as a direct text in His Book and also indicated to them what is rational in the matter, as a victory from Allah for His party and support for His religion with both types of proof, i.e., scriptural and rational. And Allah establishes the truth and abolishes falsehood, even if the criminals dislike it.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents the proof from Quran 67:13-14 that Allah creates human actions. The author, al-Nasafi, first cites the verse and then explains two aspects: the direct textual proof (نص) and the rational indication (إشارة). The direct proof is that the verse explicitly states that Allah knows what is hidden and declared, and then asks 'Does He who created not know?' This links knowledge to creation, implying that the actions known are also created by Him. The author argues that if Allah's knowledge of actions is used to confirm that He is their Creator, then the knowledge must be based on creation, making the actions created by Him. The indication is that the verse establishes Allah's knowledge of speech (concealed or public) by establishing His creation of that speech. If creation were possible without knowledge, then using creation to prove knowledge would be meaningless and foolish, like a person claiming knowledge of something based on an irrelevant personal attribute. Therefore, the creation of actions is a necessary condition for Allah's knowledge of them, and the verse proves both. The passage concludes that Allah has provided both scriptural and rational proof for this doctrine.

Key Terms
إشارة (indication)
تخليق (creation)
علم (knowledge)
حكمة (wisdom)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the rational indication is a weak or secondary argument.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows it is a necessary logical implication: the verse's structure would be absurd if creation were not involved.

Checkpoint
What analogy does al-Nasafi use to illustrate the foolishness of using creation to prove knowledge without necessity?
A) A person saying they are tall to prove they know jurisprudence
B) A person saying they are a cloth merchant's son to prove they know jurisprudence
C) A person saying they are a brave hero to prove they are knowledgeable
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The rational indication shows that the verse logically requires that Allah creates the actions He knows, making the proof both scriptural and rational.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as though every action you take—even the words you utter—is created by Allah? If so, how does that change the way you approach your daily choices and your reliance on Him?
?
The rational argument in this lesson shows that Allah's knowledge and creation are inseparably linked. If you claim to believe in Allah's all-encompassing knowledge, why do you sometimes act as if your actions are independent of His creation? What would change if you fully internalized this truth?
?
When you sin, do you reflect on the fact that Allah not only knew it but also created that action? How can this understanding deepen your repentance and your turning back to Allah, rather than making you feel trapped?
